# Created 2026-06-13 Sat 15:00
#+title: Hactar Docs
#+author: k
* Hactar Docs
** Overview
Hactar is an augmented coding assistant that lives in your editor or terminal of choice. No AI hype bullshit, no agents, no vibe coding, just a tool that helps you write, debug, and iterate on code faster. An AI coding tool for devs doing serious work in tools they’ve spent decades mastering.

Hactar's core feature is tight integration with a knowledge repository. It leverages well written, meticulously crafted developer documentation that dramatically increases the quality of code generated by SOTA models. You can think of it like devdocs + starter kits + AI assistant. The starter kit era brought into the agent era.

Hactar places an emphasis on hackability and integration. Hactar isn't a closed-source black box or a CLI designed to be used with proprietary protocols. It is a first-class citizen in your developer experience. You can modify it on the fly while you work (and it will help with those modifications). Hactar uses both LLMs and hardcode knowledge to accomplish tasks. We don't wrap things up in a Vscode fork we tightly integrate with Emacs, Neovim, and the CLI. If you are a LISPer, Rubyist etc, you will feel right at home.

Some of Hactar's features:

- *Smart Context*
  Hactar is the only AI tool integrated with a content repository (paid or bring your own). Millions of notes, error messages and solutions, examples, snippets, etc., pulled directly from realworld projects give Hactar unparalleled skills.
- *Hackable and Extensible*
  Hactar is explicitly designed to be extended while you work. When you discover gaps in the LLM's knowledge, you can patch it for later.
- *Bring Your Own Key*
  No pricing changes or being tied to any specific model. Hactar supports all major providers, from Ollama to OpenRouter.
- *Tight Ecosystem Integration*
  Hactar is for developers who live and breathe their editors. Neovim and Emacs are integrated using community standards. No Vscode forks here.
- *Agents that Never Break*
  Hactar agents don't do vibe coding. They are specifically designed to only code what works 99% of the time. Hactar agents manage configs, update dependencies, run tests, etc. These small wins add up when they work flawlessly.
- *Unix Philosophy*
  Hactar exposes the context as a file that it fully understands. You can add and drop files by writing plain text and linking to them. This makes it trivial to use everything from Emacs tooling to grep and sed to manage your context.
- *Old School Hard Coded Intelligence*
  Hactar uses "modes" to provide intelligent contextual knowledge to an LLM. With the magic of hard coding we can do things like look up docs for a React API in ms instead of seconds.
** Installation
*** Quick Start
The preferred way to run hactar is via roswell. If you have it already do:

#+begin_src sh
  ros install hactar-project/hactar
#+end_src

If you don't have roswell yet install it or use the hactar script:

#+begin_src sh
  curl -L https://hactar.space/install.sh | bash
#+end_src

Nix:

#+begin_src sh
  nix profile install "github:hactar-project/hactar"
  hactar hactar.init
#+end_src

GitHub Releases:

#+begin_src sh
  cd ~/.local/bin && wget -qO- https://github.com/hactar-project/hactar/releases/latest/download/hactar-0.1.tar.gz | tar -xz -C hactar
  hactar hactar.init
#+end_src

*Important*: You'll need to run =hactar hactar.init= if you install without running install.sh or using roswell.

Now you can run hactar in any git repo:

#+begin_src sh
  hactar
#+end_src

You'll want to set API keys. Any of the following will do:

- =OPENAI_API_KEY=: The API key for OpenAI models
- =ANTHROPIC_API_KEY=: The API key for Anthropic models
- =GEMINI_API_KEY=: he API for vertex/google ai studio
- =OPENROUTER_API_KEY=: The OpenRouter api key.

You'll likely want to set a model you can do this with an environment variable =HACTAR_MODEL=. In this case a github_copilot model:

#+begin_src sh
  env HACTAR_MODEL="copilot/gemini-3.1-pro-preview" hactar
#+end_src

Hactar comes with a several different interfaces. The default is a minimal readline tui. If you want to use Hactar with ACP pass =--acp=. To disable all tui pass =--in-editor= and you will get a minimal Hactar designed to be wrapped in an editor like Neovim or Emacs. Pass =--lit= to use Hactar literately via org-mode.
*** IDE Setup
**** Emacs
Hactar.el isn't on melpa yet so you can use the standard github method:
#+begin_src emacs-lisp
  (use-package hactar
       :straight (:host "github" :repo "hactar-project/hactar.el" :files ("*.el"))
      :config
  (setq hactar-args '("--model" "gemini/gemini-2.5-pro-preview-06-05"))
  :bind
  ("C-c h" . hactar-transient-menu)
  ("C-x g h s" . hactar-sonnet)
  ("C-x g h d" . hactar-deepseek)
  ("C-x g h g" . hactar-gemini)
  ("C-x g h t" . hactar-gemini-thinking)
  ("C-x g h o" . hactar-o3-mini))
#+end_src
**** Neovim
Hactar supports all the usual plugin managers:
***** lazy.nvim
#+begin_src lua
  {
     'hactar-project/hactar.nvim',
  ---@module 'oil'
  ---@type oil.SetupOpts
  opts = {},
  -- Optional dependencies
  dependencies = { { "echasnovski/mini.icons", opts = {} } },
  -- dependencies = { "nvim-tree/nvim-web-devicons" }, -- use if you prefer nvim-web-devicons
  -- Lazy loading is not recommended because it is very tricky to make it work correctly in all situations.
  lazy = false,
  }
#+end_src
***** Packer
#+begin_src lua
  use 'hactar-project/hactar.nvim'
#+end_src
***** Paq
#+begin_src lua
  require("paq")({
  { "hactar-project/hactar.nvim" },
  })
#+end_src
***** vim-plug
#+begin_src vim
  Plug 'hactar-project/hactar.nvim'
#+end_src
***** dein
#+begin_src vim
  call dein#add('hactar-project/hactar.nvim')
#+end_src
***** Pathogen
#+begin_src sh
  git clone --depth=1 https://github.com/hactar-project/hactar.nvim.git ~/.vim/bundle/
#+end_src
***** Manual clone
#+begin_src sh
  git clone --depth=1 https://github.com/hactar-project/hactar.nvim.git

  "${XDG_DATA_HOME:-$HOME/.local/share}"/nvim/site/pack/hactar/start/hactar.nvim
#+end_src
***** Setup
#+begin_src lua
    require('hactar').setup({
    auto_manage_context = false,
    default_bindings = false,
    debug = true,
    vim = true,
    ignore_buffers = {},

    -- only necessary if you want to change the default keybindings
    vim.api.nvim_set_keymap('n', '<leader>C', ':HactarOpen --no-auto-commits<CR>', {noremap = true, silent = true})
  })
#+end_src
**** Emacs agent-shell.el
Hactar includes ACP support and the Emacs extension provides integration with agent-shell.el. Just call =agent-shell-hactar-start= and you will be up and running. See the [[https://hactar.space/docs/emacs][Emacs extension docs]] for more details
**** Zed
Add the following to your settings.json:

#+begin_src json
  "agent_servers": {
    "Hactar": {
      "type": "custom",
      "command": "hactar",
      "args": ["--acp"],
      "env": {},
    },
  },
#+end_src
**** avante.nvim
Add the following to your lua config:

#+begin_src lua
  {
    "yetone/avante.nvim",
    event = "VeryLazy",
    version = false,
    build = "make",
    opts = {
      provider = "hactar",
      mode = "agentic",
      acp_providers = {
        hactar = {
          command = os.getenv("HOME") .. "/bin/hactar",
          args = { "--acp" },
          env = {
            HOME = os.getenv("HOME"),
            PATH = os.getenv("PATH"),
          },
        },
      },
    },
    dependencies = {
      "nvim-lua/plenary.nvim",
      "MunifTanjim/nui.nvim",
      "nvim-tree/nvim-web-devicons",
      {
        "MeanderingProgrammer/render-markdown.nvim",
        opts = {
          file_types = { "markdown", "Avante" },
        },
        ft = { "markdown", "Avante" },
      },
    },
  },
#+end_src
*** From Source
Hactar is a Common LISP project. This makes it very hackable and you might want to run it from source.

First get all the dependencies. Mainly you will just need a working quicklisp environment. This is easiest on nix, you can use the shell.nix and flake.nix.

Arch:

#+begin_src sh
  sudo pacman -Sy git sbcl readline libuv rlwrap pkg-config openssl zlib libyaml libev libevdev
#+end_src

Ubuntu:

#+begin_src sh
  sudo apt update
  sudo apt install git sbcl libreadline-dev libuv1-dev rlwrap pkg-config libssl-dev zlib1g-dev libyaml-dev libev-dev
#+end_src

Now you can run =make build= to get a build of it. The build script should download all the quicklisp dependencies for you.

Hactar will be built to ./bin/hactar. Please report any issues you run into and read the development guide.
** Hactar Glossary
*** Core Concepts
- Rules :: Rules are how the system prompt is changed in response to code
- Analyzers :: Handle parsing code and extracting details like =is-react?=
- Processors :: Take user input and LLM output and do something with it
- Slash Commands :: Slash commands are the primary interactive mechanism in the Hactar REPL e.g =/add= for adding files
- Dot Commands :: Dot commands operate on the context/prompt itself. e.g .mod! to make code changes
- Modes :: how Hactar changes the behavior of commands based on context and environment
*** Useful Terms to Know
- MCP :: Model Context Protocol -- this the standard for tool calling that LLM providers have settled on.
- ACP :: Agent Context Protocol -- An extension of MCP for agents
** Hactar Cheatsheet
*** How to get Help?
Hactar is developed on GitHub and the primary route for help is via Discussions and Issues. You can also hop into the Discord and ask questions.

When reporting issues please include info like hactar version, model, settings etc. You can get all the info like version, model, context, settings etc with the =/dump= command.
*** Installing a Hactar Extension
Hactar extensions are simple lisp files that get copied into a folder. Similar to the extension system you find in Emacs or Neovim ecosystems.

To install one simply clone it onto your path somewhere (e.g "~/.config/hactar/plugins~") and add it to your hactar.lisp:

#+begin_src lisp
  (load "myplugin/core.lisp")
#+end_src

You can manage your plugins using git. Here is an example make file to update all plugins:

#+begin_src makefile
  PLUGINS_DIR ?= ~/.config/hactar/plugins

  update-plugins:
          @echo "Updating plugins in $(PLUGINS_DIR)..."
          @for dir in $(PLUGINS_DIR)/*; do \
                  if [ -d "$$dir/.git" ]; then \
                          echo "--> Updating $$dir"; \
                          (cd "$$dir" && git pull); \
                  fi \
          done
          @echo "Done."

  .PHONY: update-plugins
#+end_src
*** How to use Comments to Trigger Hactar to Make Changes?
Pass the =--watch= flag to hactar and then use the following syntax in comments

- =AI!=: Trigger hactar to make changes. Describe the changes in the comment line and following lines.
- =AI?=: Trigger hactar to anwser questions about the code.
*** Generating a Repo Map
Use the scan command =hactar scan=

You can pass the format flag to control what hactar outputs. For example, here is how to generate an org-mode file describing the API of the codebase:

#+begin_src lisp
  hactar scan -f org-mode
#+end_src
*** What Models and Model types are used in Hactar?
Hactar has three model types:

- main/current/default model: This is the default model used for most tasks
- cheap-model: This is the model used for programmatic and architecture tasks. For example, to generate JSON meta data from documentation.
- embedding-model: The model used for embedding

You can list available models with:

=/models=
*** Adding Instructions for Hactar to Context?
You can use an =AGENTS.md=, =AGENTS.org=, =.hactar.guide.md=, or =.hactar.guide.org= in the project's root. It will be added to context
*** Where is the model config stored?
In =$XDG_CONFIG_DIR/hactar/models.yaml=.
*** Where are the prompts stored?
In =$XDG_CONFIG_DIR/hactar/prompts=.
*** How are docs automatically loaded into Hactar?
Hactar accomplishes smart context using what we call modes. Modes work with specific filetypes and use old school techniques like parsing and regex to determine what your code is, what you are doing, and what context you might need. LISP allows us to build up this using a DSL. For example, want to check you are in a React project and then add React api docs? Just a good old call to a function =is-project-react?=.

Why not something like skills triggers? Or rules? The same reason we also eschew MCP, it keeps the context smaller. In other CLI tools automatic loading of e.g skills is accomplished by the LLM. This means you are constantly giving up context to listing out available skills, docs, etc. Not only are you giving up context but you are adding latency by requiring extra calls to an LLM.

Using actual code to add stuff to context allows us to load things into context without sacrifices.
*** Adding API Documentation to Hactar
You have three options for adding API docs:

1. Importing the docs file into the database with the =/docs.import= command. *Note*: They will ned to follow the  [[#api-docs-format][API Format]]
2. With a defdoc macro.
3. Just adding the file with /add

The last is the most simple and for one off things just using =/add= is fine.

The most powerful route is the =defdoc= macro. You can define where the docs are in code and then use LISP and Hactar features to intelligently add an remove docs.

Here is an example of that:

#+begin_src lisp
  (defdoc "Latest React Docs" :source "hactar:docsets/react.19.2.3.org" :version "latest")
#+end_src

If you want to for example listen to stack changes and dynamically add docs depending on what you are working on you can use hooks. Here is an example of that:

#+begin_src lisp
  (defun update-stripe-docs (&rest args)
    (declare (ignore args))
    (defdoc "Stripe API Reference"
      :source (cond
                ((member "go" *stack* :test #'string=) "hactar:docsets/stripe.go.latest.org")
                ((member "node" *stack* :test #'string=) "hactar:docsets/stripe.node.latest.org")
                ((member "ruby" *stack* :test #'string=) "hactar:docsets/stripe.ruby.latest.org")
                (t "hactar:docsets/stripe.curl.latest.org"))
      :uri "stripe-api-docs"
      :version "latest"))

  (nhooks:add-hook *stack-changed-hook* (make-instance 'nhooks:handler :fn #'update-stripe-docs :name 'stripe-docs-update))
  (update-stripe-docs)
#+end_src
Once you have docs in Hactar you can use =/docs-add= to search through them and add to context. Or you can write rules and hooks to add them automatically.

API docs can be in any format but if they are in org-mode and follow some conventions then Hactar can do things like slice up the API docs so only specific parts are added to context. This can be very useful for reducing token usage. See the docs for the [[#api-docs-format][API Format]] for more info.
*** Using Agent Skills with Hactar
Hactar has partial support for agent skills. We say partial because in Hactar you have to load agent skills manually. We do this intentionally to reduce token usage, increase model performance, and reduce LLM queries.

Load a skill into context using =skills.load <name> [--forms] [--ref]=. Add a skill using =skills.add= e.g =hactar skills.add anthropics/skills skills=.

Skills Commands:

#+begin_src sh
  skills.list                        - List available skills
  skills.search                      - Search skills and load one
  skills.load <name> [--forms] [--ref] - Load a skill into context
  skills.add <source>                - Add a skill from a source
  skills.validate <path>             - Validate a skill directory or name
  skills.doc [format]                - Generate documentation for available skills
  skills.help                        - Show this help message
#+end_src
*** How to use Hactar in an ACP client?
Pass the =--acp= flag to enable ACP mode.
*** How to ignore all the Hactar stuff?
- Ignore all of it with =*.hactar=
- Ignore context files with =.hactar*.context.org=
- Ignore port files with =.hactar*.port=
- Ignore transcripts with =.hactar*.transcript.json=
- Ignore session files with =.hactar*.session.lisp=
*** How to theme the TUI?
Use the =hactar:make-tui-theme= function:

Example:

#+begin_src lisp
  (hactar:make-tui-theme
   :name "catppuccin-mocha"
   :bg "#1e1e2e" :fg "#cdd6f4"
   :border "#585b70" :border-accent "#89b4fa"
   :header "#f5c2e7" :header-bold "#f5c2e7"
   :selected-fg "#1e1e2e" :selected-bg "#f5c2e7"
   :muted "#6c7086" :prompt-marker "#89b4fa"
   :status-info-fg "#cdd6f4" :status-info-bg nil
   :status-ok-fg "#1e1e2e" :status-ok-bg "#a6e3a1"
   :status-error-fg "#cdd6f4" :status-error-bg "#f38ba8"
   :sidebar-title "#f5c2e7" :sidebar-label "#89b4fa"
   :file-added "#a6e3a1" :file-removed "#f38ba8"
   :modal-bg-fg "#cdd6f4" :modal-bg-bg "#313244"
   :modal-border "#89b4fa"
   :modal-input-fg "#cdd6f4" :modal-input-bg "#45475a"
   :tab-active-fg "#1e1e2e" :tab-active-bg "#f5c2e7"
   :tab-inactive-fg "#6c7086" :tab-inactive-bg nil
   :keyhint "#89b4fa"
   :lsp-ok "#a6e3a1"
   :tool-pending "#f9e2af" :tool-running "#89b4fa"
   :tool-done "#a6e3a1" :tool-failed "#f38ba8"
   :chat-user "#89b4fa" :chat-assistant nil
   :chat-thought "#6c7086" :chat-bash "#a6e3a1" :chat-error "#f38ba8"
   :completion-fg "#cdd6f4" :completion-bg "#313244")
#+end_src
** Usage
The main workflow for hactar is:

- Run it in a github project =hactar=
- Add files using =/add=
- Type instructions/prompt
- Hactar generates git patches and applies them based on the prompt
*** Rules
Hactar can be extended with rules. The simplest form of rules is just a file named .hactar.rules. This will be added to the context automatically.

This isn't particulary useful though. To make rules useful you need to have them triggered by something. Hactar provides a large variety of hooks and triggers for rules. Let's apply a rule when the project stack contains react:

#+begin_src lisp
  (defrule :prefer-custom-hooks
   "Prefer custom hooks over libraries where possible."
   :triggers '(:stack (:react)))
#+end_src

Hactar is pretty good at extending itself. You can give rule generation a try with the =/gen-rule= command. Hactar will attempt to write a rule for based on your instructions. Then it will add it to your user.lisp file. Please read any rules it generates first and don't blindly accept them.
*** Docs
A core feature of Hactar is tight integration with a repository of reference docs. Most of the time documentation is automatically added to context as needed. You can manually add docs using =/docs-add= and you can drop docs from context using =/docs-drop= (or =/drop=).
**** /docs
List known documentation relevant to the current project stack. Basically uses =*docs*= global. If you want to lookup all documentation not just relevant ones use =/docs-db= and =/search-add-files=
**** /docs-add
Add documentation from file, URL, package name (@p/name@ver), or fzf selection. Optionally include metadata:

#+begin_src sh
  /docs-add <source> -tags=js -covers=react
#+end_src
**** /docs-ask
Ask the LLM to find documentation for a query, fetch it, and add it.
**** /docs-clear
Delete all documents from the database (requires confirmation).
**** /docs-context
Show documentation currently added to the context.
**** /docs-find
Search documentation database by text query and add selected doc to context.
**** /docs-guess
Guess relevant documentation based on the last added file's content.
**** /docs-gen
Generate documentation for the current context using the LLM.
*** Errors
Hactar maintains a database of errors and solutions. You can import errors from org-mode files or add them manually.
**** /errors
Find and select errors relevant to the current project/context.
**** /errors-add
Add a new error entry manually.
**** /errors-find
Search in DB using a query and add selected to context.
**** /errors-db
List all known error docs and select one to add to context.
**** /errors.import
Import an error document (Org format).
*** Modes
Modes are how Hactar hard codes knowledge instead of relying on an LLM for every little thing. Modes let Hactar know how to look up API docs and tooling specific to the type of project you are working on. Hactar for example, can detect when a React project is being worked on then automatically add the React API docs and list of links to tutorials. A mode is a collection of prompts, analyzers, processors, hooks, and custom hardcoded dev tooling. Think LSP if it was developed in the LLM era.

You can manually enable and disable modes with =/mode=. You can list currently enabled modes with =/modes=.
*** Analyzers
Analyzers take code files an analyze them using a combination of hard coded and LLM models. By default they get enabled and disable automatically by modes.
*** Processors
Processors in Hactar handle processing the output from the LLMs.

For example here is the code that handles search and replace responses
#+begin_src lisp
  (def-processor search-replace-processor (history)
                 "Parses and applies SEARCH/REPLACE blocks from the last assistant message."
                 (when history
                   (let ((last-message (car (last history))))
                     (when (string= (cdr (assoc :role last-message)) "assistant")
                       (let* ((content (cdr (assoc :content last-message)))
                              (blocks (parse-search-replace-blocks content)))
                         (when blocks
                           (format t "~&Applying ~A SEARCH/REPLACE block(s)...~%" (length blocks))
                           (apply-search-replace-blocks blocks)
                           (format t "~&Finished applying blocks.~%")))))))
#+end_src
*** Guides
Guides are READMEs for agents. A lot like Claude.md or AGENTS.md but in Hactar they are smart and hooked up to a knowledge repository. You can think of it like those developer guides for a stack. They cover everything from best practices, how to write tests for that specific stack, to API documentation.

Hactar doesn't just add these files to your context, it includes first class tooling for writing, editing, modifying, and slicing them up. It has special agent features and prompts to intelligently add and modify them.

You can add one to your current project by writing a =AGENTS.md=, =AGENTS.org=, =.hactar.guide.org=, =.hactar.guide.md=. By default it assumes you only want to load one and =.hactar.guide= will be prioritized.

The global =XDG_CONFIG_DIR/hactar/.hactar.org= will be loaded together with any project specific one.
**** Guides Commands
***** /guide
Print the content of the currently active guide file.
***** /guide-add-api
Search docs tagged 'api', select one, and add/update it under the 'APIs' (:apis:) headline.
***** /guide-add-docs
Search docs tagged 'docs', select one, and add/update it under the 'Documentation' (:docs:) headline.
***** /guide-add-example
Search docs tagged 'example', select one, and add/update it under the 'Examples' (:examples:) headline.
***** /guides
List available *.guide.* files and select one to activate.
***** /guides-gen
Generate or update the .hactar.guide.* file using the LLM.
***** /guides-update
Update the .hactar.guide.* file using the LLM based on the current context.
*** Agents
Agents in hactar are instances of hactar that act on a task in a loop with REPL. For example, you might have a lint agent that automatically fixes lint issues.

Hactar comes wih several built in agents and is designed to make building new agents quick and easy. Often you can even have Hactar one shot generate you a new specific agent.

You run agents with the command =/agent-run= or =agent.run=. Agents are a simple function created using the =defagent= macro.

Example:

#+begin_src sh
  hactar agent.run cmd "bun run typecheck"
#+end_src
**** cmd agent
Runs a command, and if it fails, asks an LLM for a fix and retries up to 3 times. Other agents like lint, typecheck etc are built ontop of the cmd agent.
***** Usage
#+begin_src sh
  hactar agent.run cmd "bun run typecheck"
#+end_src
**** test agent
Runs a test command in a loop and fixes code with test failures using SEARCH/REPLACE blocks.
***** Usage
Run it:

#+begin_src sh
  hactar agent.run test
#+end_src
****** Configure
You can configure the test command in your =.hactar.toml= =project.commands.test=:

#+begin_src toml
  [project.commands]
  test = "bun run test"
#+end_src
By default Hactar will try to guess your test command based on stack and files in context.
***** Tips
- You can use =gen.project.config= to automatically generate a project config with the correct test command. That way you don't need to keep adding stuff like package.json to the context.
**** typecheck agent
Runs a typecheck command in a loop and fixes code with failures using SEARCH/REPLACE blocks.
***** Usage
Run it:

#+begin_src sh
  hactar agent.run typecheck
#+end_src
****** Configure
You can configure the typecheck command in your =.hactar.toml= =project.commands.typecheck=:

#+begin_src toml
  [project.commands]
  typecheck = "bun run typecheck"
#+end_src
By default Hactar will try to guess your typecheck command based on stack and files in context.
***** Tips
- You can use =gen.project.config= to automatically generate a project config with the correct typecheck command. That way you don't need to keep adding stuff like package.json to the context.
**** lint agent
Runs a lint command in a loop and fixes code with lint failures using SEARCH/REPLACE blocks.
***** Usage
Run it:

#+begin_src sh
  hactar agent.run lint
#+end_src
****** Configure
You can configure the lint command in your =.hactar.toml= =project.commands.lint=:

#+begin_src toml
  [project.commands]
  lint = "bun run lint"
#+end_src
By default Hactar will try to guess your lint command based on stack and files in context.
***** Tips
- You can use =gen.project.config= to automatically generate a project config with the correct lint command. That way you don't need to keep adding stuff like package.json to the context.
*** Flags/Options
**** --tui
A flag to enable a full ncurses based tui. By default it is disabled so integration in your editor of choice is easier.
**** --assistant
Enable assistant mode for visual interaction.
**** --audio
Enable TTS audio output for assistant's extractions (used with --assistant).
**** --author VALUE
Author name. Defaults to the value of the =HACTAR_AUTHOR= environment variable.
**** --auto-all
Enable all agent-like auto features (--auto-lint, --auto-test, --auto-typecheck).
**** --auto-lint
Enable automatic linting after code changes.
**** --auto-test
Enable automatic testing after code changes.
**** --auto-typecheck
Enable automatic type checking after code changes.
**** --disable-analyzers VALUE
List of analyzers to disable (space-separated). [default:]
**** --enable-analyzers VALUE
List of analyzers to enable (space-separated). [default:]
**** --embedding-model Value
Set the model used for generating embeddings default to =nomic-embed-text=.

*Gotcha*: The embedding model is ollama only. Do not prefix the model.
**** --execute-immediately VALUE
Generate a shell command from the query, execute it, and print its output.
**** --help
Display usage information and exit.
**** --http-port INT
Port for the HTTP API server [default: 4269]
**** --live-dangerously
Turns off all the features that prevent hactar from destroying your codebase or system. Not available except as a flag. It allows Hactar to run as an agent without being in a vm, without a git respository, and execute any commands the LLM decides it wants to. Don't use please.
**** --name VALUE
Project name. Defaults to current directory name.
**** --output VALUE
File path to write assistant's text extractions (used with --assistant).
**** --version
Display version and exit.
**** -c, --config-path VALUE
Path to the models configuration file (models.yaml)
**** -e, --execute VALUE
Generate a shell command from the query, print it, and copy it to clipboard.
**** -m, --model VALUE
LLM model to use (e.g., ollama/qwen3:14b) [default: ollama/qwen3:14b]
**** -p, --slynk-port INT
Port for the Slynk server [default: 4005]
**** -q, --query VALUE
Send a query to the LLM, print the result, and exit.
**** -w, --watch
Watch files and make code changes when =AI= comments are detected.

- A comment with =AI!= will trigger code changes
- A comment with =AI?= can be used to ask questions
**** --acp
Enable the ACP mode and interface. This will cause hactar to return all output via JSON-RPC on stdout and accept input as json-rpc
**** --lisp
Enable a lisp-rpc mode. This will cause hactar to return all output as LISP forms on stdout and accept input as LISP.
**** --lit
Enable literate mode. This lets you edit all Hactar context via org-mode.
**** Model Shortcuts
***** --gemini
Use Gemini Pro 2.5 (gemini/gemini-2.5-pro-exp-03-25)
***** --gemini-free
Use free Gemini Pro Experimental via OpenRouter (openrouter/google/gemini-2.5-pro-exp-03-25:free)
***** --sonnet
Use Anthropic Sonnet model (anthropic/claude-3-7-sonnet-20250219)
***** --o4
Use OpenAI GPT-4o Mini model (openai/o4-mini)
***** --deepseek
Use Deepseek Chat model via OpenRouter (openrouter/deepseek/deepseek-chat-v3-0324)
***** --deepseek-free
Use free Deepseek Base model via OpenRouter (openrouter/deepseek/deepseek-v3-base:free)
*** Commands
Hactar commands are divided into three types:

- slash commands. these are hactar commands and change the state of hactar e.g =/add=
- dot commands operate on the context and instruct the LLM. They might for example, create a new file.
- hactar sub commands. These are commands you pass to hactar on startup e.g =create=
**** Subcommands
***** hactar.init
Initialize Hactar: clone repo and install default prompts and models.
***** acp
Start Hactar in Agent Client Protocol (ACP) mode over stdio.
***** agent.run
Run an agent by name.

Usage:
#+begin_src sh
  hactar agent.run <agent_name> [agent_args...]
#+end_src
***** agent.stop
Stop a running agent by its ID.

Usage:
#+begin_src sh
  hactar agent.stop <agent_id>
#+end_src
***** agents
List currently running agents.
***** browse
Browse web pages as plaintext.

Supported route:
- =browse <url> [--format markdown|org]= — Fetch and convert a URL to plaintext.
***** check
Run environment and setup checks and exit with appropriate status.
***** check-file
Check source files for issues and output diagnostics.

Usage:
#+begin_src sh
  hactar check-file file1.lisp [file2.lisp ...] [-f format]
#+end_src

Target is auto-detected from =(target :xxx)= declarations in source files. Formats: =xml= (default), =json=.
***** code.index
Index the codebase using ctags.
***** compile
Compile Lisp source files to a target language.

Usage:
#+begin_src sh
  hactar compile file1.lisp [file2.lisp ...] [-o output-dir] [-f format] [--dry]
#+end_src

Target is auto-detected from =(target :xxx)= declarations in source files. If =--format= is set, outputs in that format (=org=, =lisp=). Otherwise flushes to =--output= dir. If neither =--format= nor =--output= is set, defaults to dry run with =<file>= tag output.
***** component.create
Create a new component.
***** component.list
List all components.
***** copilotapi
GitHub Copilot API commands: models, authorize, complete.
***** create
Create a new project from a starter.

Usage:
#+begin_src sh
  hactar create --path <dir> --starter <starter> <prompt...>
#+end_src
***** help
Display comprehensive help information about Hactar.
***** check
Run environment and setup checks and exit with appropriate status.
***** docs-import
Import a text file into the documentation database.
***** docs.db
List all known documentation in the dataabase and select one. In non-interactive mode, prints the path of the selected doc.
***** errors.db
Alias for =errors-db=.
***** feature
Activate or manage features.

Usage:
#+begin_src sh
  hactar feature <name> [-v/--variant <variant>]
  hactar feature list
  hactar feature active
  hactar feature off <name>
  hactar feature show <name>
  hactar feature --dry-run <name>
#+end_src

***** frameworkroute.list

#+end_src

***** help
Display comprehensive help information about Hactar.
***** hn
Fetch news from news.ycombinator.com (Hacker News).

Supported routes:
- =newest= — Fetch newest posts from Hacker News.
- =top= — Fetch top posts from Hacker News.

Usage:

#+end_src

Options:
- =-m, --model MODEL= — LLM model to use
- =-f, --format FORMAT= — Output format (=markdown= or =org=)
- =--clear-cache= — Clear the cache

**** Slash Commands
***** /!
Run a shell command and optionally add the output to the chat.
***** /add
Add files or images to the chat. If no arguments are given, uses fzf to select a file. Can provide image descriptions via =-descriptions="desc1,desc2"=.
***** /agent
Interact with a monolith agent.

Usage:
#+begin_src
  /agent <name> <task>
#+end_src

Available agents: =librarian=, =architect=, =implementer=, =critic=.
***** /agent-run
Run an agent. With no arguments, it shows a selector. Otherwise, runs the agent named in the first argument.
***** /agent-stop
Select and stop a running agent.
***** /allow
Add a session override to always allow a tool.

Usage:
#+begin_src
  /allow <tool_name>
#+end_src
***** /ask
Ask questions about the code base without editing any files.
***** /assistant-update
Manually trigger assistant screen analysis with an optional prompt.
***** /autocommit
Toggle git autocommit on/off.

Alias for =/ruhe-summary=.

Usage:
#+begin_src
  /brief [length]
#+end_src

Set the cheap model to use when cost is a concern.

#+end_src

***** /context.expose
Expose the current context to =hactar.{pid}.context.org= and keep it synchronized:

- Adds/removes src blocks under the =Files= headline when files are added/dropped.
- Automatically updates block contents when files change on disk.
- Syncs project variables to =Project Details= section.

***** /docs
Find and select documentation relevant to the current project stack. In non-interactive mode, prints the path of the selected doc.

The =*docs*= global is considered to always be relevant to current stack. When there are no docs in =*docs*= we query the DB. Use =/docs-db= to always select from the DB.

Usage:
#+begin_src
  /docs [--format=json]
#+end_src

#+end_src
