***** Components
****** globals
******* General State
These variables manage the general operational state of Hactar.
- =*hactar-version*=: The version of the Hactar application (Default: ="0.1.0"=).
- =*debug-stream*=: Stream for debug output (Default: =nil=).
- =*debug*=: Enable debug output (Default: =nil=).
- =*silent*=: Suppress non-essential output when T (Default: =nil=).
- =*in-repl*=: True if currently inside the interactive REPL (Default: =nil=).
- =*in-editor*=: True if hactar is being run inside an editor (Default: =nil=, set via =--in-editor= flag or =HACTAR_IN_EDITOR= env var).
- =*editor-log-file*=: Pathname to the .hactar.{pid}.log file used for structured output in editor mode (Default: =nil=).
******* Project Metadata
- =*name*=: The name of the project (Default: =nil=).
- =*author*=: The author of the project (Default: =HACTAR_AUTHOR= env var or =nil=).
- =*repo-root*=: The root directory of the repository being watched (Default: =nil=).
- =*stack*=: A list of technologies used in the stack (Default: ='()=).
- =*stack-changed-hook*=: Hook run when the stack changes. Handlers receive the new stack as argument.
- =*shell*=: The shell being used on the system (Default: =HACTAR_SHELL= or =SHELL= env vars, fallback ="bash"=).
- =*language*=: The main language being used in the project (Default: ="unknown"=).
- =*repo-map*=: A map of all the symbols and tags in the current project. Generated using tree-sitter (Default: =nil=).
******* Models
- =*model-changed-hook*=: Hook run when *current-model* changes. Handler is called with (new-model old-model).
- =*current-model*=: The current model being used (Default: =nil=).
- =*embedding-model*=: Model to use for generating embeddings (Default: ="nomic-embed-text"=).
- =*completion-model*=: Model configuration specifically for the /complete command and endpoint (Default: =HACTAR_COMPLETION_MODEL= env var or ="ollama/minimax-m2.5:cloud"=).
- =*chunking-llm*=: Model configuration specifically for chunk processing tasks (Default: =HACTAR_CHUNKING_MODEL= env var or ="ollama/minimax-m2.5:cloud"=).
- =*cheap-model*=: The cheap model to use when cost is more of a concern (Default: =HACTAR_CHEAP_MODEL= env var or ="ollama/minimax-m2.5:cloud"=).
- =*docs-meta-model*=: Model to use for generating documentation metadata (Default: =HACTAR_DOCS_META_MODEL= env var, fallback to =*cheap-model*=).
- =*available-models*=: List of available models (Default: =nil=).
******* Chat & Context
- =*chat-history*=: The chat history (Default: ='()=).
- =*chat-history-limit*=: Maximum character limit for chat history (Default: =8000=).
- =*multiline-mode*=: Whether multiline mode is enabled (Default: =nil=).
- =*transcript-file*=: File to save chat transcript to (Default: =".hactar.transcript.json"=).
- =*file-watcher*=: The global file watcher instance (Default: =nil=).
- =*files*=: Files currently in the context window. Synchronized with context file (Default: =nil=).
- =*images*=: List of images currently in the context (Default: ='()=).
- =*docs-context*=: List of documentation plists currently added to the context (Default: ='()=).
- =*docs*=: Global list of defined documentation (Default: =nil=).
- =*docs-folder*=: Default folder to look for documentation files (Default: ="docs/"=).
- =*errors-context*=: List of error plists currently added to the context (Default: ='()=).
- =*errors*=: Global list of defined errors (Default: =nil=).
******* Paths & Configuration
- =*hactar-repo-url*=: The Git URL for the Hactar project repository (Default: =HACTAR_REPO_URL= env var or ="git@github.com:hactar-project/hactar.git"=).
- =*hactar-repo-dir*=: The local directory for the Hactar project repository (Default: =HACTAR_REPO_DIR= env var or =~/.local/share/hactar-repo/=).
- =*hactar-data-path*=: Path to Hactar's data dir (Default: =HACTAR_DATA_PATH= env var or =~/.local/share/hactar/=).
- =*hactar-config-path*=: Path to Hactar's configuration directory (Default: =HACTAR_CONFIG_PATH= env var or =~/.config/hactar/=).
- =*db-path*=: Path to the SQLite database file (Default: =HACTAR_DB_PATH= env var or =*hactar-data-path*/hactar.db=).
- =*hactar-pro-path*=: Path to the Hactar Pro content repository (Default: =HACTAR_PRO_PATH= env var or =*hactar-data-path*/pro/=).
- =*hactar-starters-agent*=: Path to the default Agent starter template (Default: =HACTAR_STARTERS_AGENT_PATH= env var or =*hactar-data-path*/starters/AgentStarter.org=).
******* Limits & Constraints
- =*max-content-chars*=: Maximum character length for content before splitting (Default: =30000=).
- =*image-max-size-mb*=: Maximum size for an image file in megabytes before warning (Default: =1=).
- =*guide-warn-chars*=: Character limit for guide content before warning (Default: =30000=).
- =*guide-max-chars*=: Maximum character limit for guide content (Default: =100000=).
******* Git & File System
- =*git-autocommit*=: Enable automatic git commits after applying changes (Default: =t=).
- =*hactar-ignored-paths*=: List of regex patterns for paths to ignore (Default: ='("^\\./straight/repos/.*")=).
******* Ctags
- =*exclude-from-ctags*=: List of patterns to exclude from ctags indexing (Default: ='(".git" "node_modules" "dist" "build" "straight" "*.min.js" "*.map")=).
- =*ctags-file*=: Path to the ctags file relative to repo root (Default: =".tags"=).
- =*tags-cache*=: Cache of loaded tags (Default: =nil=).
******* Guides & Rules
- =*active-rules*=: Hash table storing the text of currently active rules (Default: =(make-hash-table :test 'equal)=).
- =*active-guide-file*=: Pathname of the currently active guide file (Default: =nil=).
- =*guide-file-extension*=: Default file extension for generated guides (Default: ="org"=).
- =*guide-exclude-tags*=: List of tags to exclude headlines from the active guide file (Default: ='("nocontext")=).
- =*hactar-guide-path*=: Path to the guide file (Default: =HACTAR_GUIDE_PATH= env var).
******* Tools
- =*defined-tools*=: Hash table storing defined tools (Default: =(make-hash-table :test 'equal)=).
- =*tool-use-enabled*=: When T, tools are available for use by the LLM (Default: =t=).
- =*tools-in-system-prompt*=: When T, include tool definitions in the system prompt (Default: =t=, unless =HACTAR_TOOLS_IN_SYSTEM_PROMPT= env var is ="false"=).
- =*hactar-skills-path*=: Path to the skills directory (Default: =HACTAR_SKILLS_PATH= env var or =*hactar-data-path*/skills/=).
- =*skills-file-ext*=: Default file extension for skill files (Default: ="md"=).
******* Permissions
- =*permission-rules*=: Ordered list of permission-rule structs (Default: ='()=).
- =*session-overrides*=: List of session-override structs created from interactive confirmations (Default: ='()=).
- =*permission-log*=: Log of recent permission decisions for debugging (Default: ='()=).
- =*safe-command-patterns*=: List of regex patterns for commands considered safe (Default: ='()=).
- =*permission-log-max*=: Maximum number of entries to keep in the permission log (Default: =100=).
******* Agent State
- =*agent-definitions*=: Hash table storing agent definitions keyed by name (Default: =(make-hash-table :test 'equal)=).
- =*running-agents*=: Hash table storing active agent instances, keyed by a unique ID (Default: =(make-hash-table :test 'equal)=).
- =*agent-retry-limit*=: Default retry limit for agents (Default: =10=).
- =*live-dangerously*=: Set to T to allow agents to run without a safe environment (Default: =nil=).
- =*agent-safe-env*=: Set to T if running in a container or other safe environment (Default: =nil=).
******* Auto-features State
- =*auto-lint*=: Enable/disable automatic linting agent (Default: =nil=).
- =*auto-test*=: Enable/disable automatic testing agent (Default: =nil=).
- =*auto-typecheck*=: Enable/disable automatic type checking agent (Default: =nil=).
- =*auto-docs*=: Enable/disable automatic documentation features (Default: =nil=).
- =*auto-suggest-commands*=: Enable/disable automatic command suggestion (Default: =nil=).
- =*auto-cmds*=: Enable/disable automatic execution of shell commands (Default: =nil=).
******* Assistant Mode State
- =*assistant-mode-active*=: Is the assistant mode currently active? (Default: =nil=).
- =*assistant-extraction*=: The last text extracted by the assistant mode LLM (Default: =nil=).
- =*assistant-last-screenshot-path*=: Pathname of the last screenshot taken by the assistant (Default: =nil=).
- =*assistant-output-file*=: Pathname to write assistant extractions to (Default: =nil=).
- =*assistant-audio-enabled*=: Is TTS audio generation enabled for assistant mode? (Default: =nil=).
- =*assistant-audio-muted*=: Is assistant mode audio output currently muted? (Default: =nil=).
- =*assistant-last-audio-file*=: Pathname of the last TTS audio file generated (Default: =nil=).
- =*piper-model-path*=: Path to the Piper TTS model (Default: =PIPER_MODEL_PATH= env var or =~/.config/hactar/speech/models/en_US-amy-low.onnx=).
- =*assistant-initial-delay-done*=: Has the initial 30s delay for assistant mode passed? (Default: =nil=).
- =*assistant-previous-image-description*=: Default description for assistant screenshots (Default: ="Screenshot of the currently focused window."=).
******* AI Comment Analyzer State
- =*ai-comment-queue*=: Queue of files with AI! comments to process (Default: ='()=).
- =*ai-comment-processor-lock*=: Lock to ensure single-threaded AI! comment processing (Default: =(bt:make-lock "ai-comment-processor-lock")=).
******* HTTP Server State
- =*http-port*=: Port for the HTTP server (Default: =4269=).
- =*http-server*=: Instance of the running Clack server (Default: =nil=).
******* Slynk Server State
- =*slynk-port*=: Port for the Slynk server (Default: =4005=).
- =*slynk-started*=: T if Slynk server has been started (Default: =nil=).
******* Watcher State
- =*watcher-definitions*=: Hash table storing watcher definitions keyed by name (Default: =(make-hash-table :test 'equal)=).
- =*active-watchers*=: Hash table storing active watcher instances (Default: =(make-hash-table :test 'equalp)=).
- =*test-command*=: Default command to run for the test watcher (Default: ="make test"=).
- =*lint-command*=: Lint command to run for the lint agent (Default: =nil=).
- =*typecheck-command*=: Typecheck command to run for the typecheck agent (Default: =nil=).
- =*test-agent-command*=: Test command to run for the test agent (Default: =nil=).
******* Context Expose State
- =*exposed-context-file*=: Pathname of the exposed context file (Default: =nil=).
- =*context-expose-hooks-installed*=: Whether context.expose hooks are installed (Default: =nil=).
- =*litmode-enabled*=: When T, literate single-file mode is active and provides context (Default: =nil=).
******* Preset System State
- =*presets*=: Hash table of defined presets (Default: =(make-hash-table :test 'equal)=).
- =*active-presets*=: List of currently active preset names (Default: ='()=).
- =*snapshots*=: Hash table of saved context snapshots (Default: =(make-hash-table :test 'equal)=).
- =*preset-search-paths*=: List of directories to search for preset files (Default: ='()=).
- =*snapshots-dir*=: Directory for storing context snapshots (Default: =~/.local/share/hactar/snapshots/=).
******* Code-Value System State
- =*code-values*=: Registry of all code-values by ID or name (Default: =(make-hash-table :test 'equal)=).
- =*code-value-counter*=: Counter for generating unique code-value IDs (Default: =0=).
- =*staged-code-values*=: List of code-values staged for application (Default: ='()=).
- =*code-value-history*=: History of applied code-value operations for undo support (Default: ='()=).
- =*code-value-history-limit*=: Maximum number of operations to keep in history (Default: =100=).
- =*transforms*=: Registry of defined transforms by name (Default: =(make-hash-table :test 'equal)=).
- =*framework-analyzers*=: Registry of framework-specific analyzers (Default: =(make-hash-table :test 'equal)=).
- =*recipes*=: Registry of defined recipes by name (Default: =(make-hash-table :test 'equal)=).
- =*template-search-paths*=: List of directories to search for templates, in priority order (Default: Parsed from =HACTAR_TEMPLATE_SEARCH_PATHS= env var or ='()=).
******* Lisp-RPC State
- =*lisp-rpc-mode*=: T when running in Lisp-RPC mode (--lisp flag) (Default: =nil=).
- =*lisp-rpc-pending-permission*=: Plist of the current pending permission request (Default: =nil=).
- =*lisp-rpc-permission-lock*=: Lock for permission condition variable (Default: =nil=).
- =*lisp-rpc-permission-cv*=: Condition variable for permission response signalling (Default: =nil=).
- =*lisp-rpc-permission-timeout*=: Seconds to wait for a permission response (Default: =120=).
******* MCP Protocol State
- =*mcp-mode*=: T when running as an MCP server over stdio (Default: =nil=).
- =*mcp-initialized*=: T after the MCP initialize handshake is complete (Default: =nil=).
******* ACP Protocol State
- =*acp-mode*=: T when running in ACP stdio mode (Default: =nil=).
- =*acp-session-id*=: The current ACP session ID (Default: =nil=).
- =*acp-client-capabilities*=: Alist of client capabilities from initialize (Default: =nil=).
- =*acp-pending-requests*=: Hash table of pending outbound requests to Client (Default: =(make-hash-table :test 'equal)=).
- =*acp-request-counter*=: Counter for generating unique outbound request IDs (Default: =0=).
- =*acp-cancelled*=: T when the current prompt turn has been cancelled (Default: =nil=).
- =*acp-initialized*=: T after the initialize handshake is complete (Default: =nil=).
******* Misc State
- =*process-history-hook*=: Hook run after chat history is updated with an LLM response (Default: =(make-instance 'nhooks:hook)=).
- =*agentshell-mode*=: T when running in AgentShell (ACP client) mode (Default: =nil=).
- =*lisp-mode-enabled*=: T when lisp mode enabled (Default: =nil=).
****** commands.lisp
******* Variables
- =*commands*= :: Hash table of registered slash commands.
- =*sub-commands*= :: Hash table of registered CLI subcommands.
- =*command-completions*= :: Hash table of completion functions keyed by command name.
- =*acp-commands*= :: Hash table of ACP-compatible command handlers.
******* Core Functions
******** =%command-fn-name=
#+begin_src lisp
  (%command-fn-name prefix name-key)
#+end_src

Generate an interned symbol name for an internal command function.

- =prefix= :: Namespace prefix like =\"SLASH-CMD\"=
- =name-key= :: Normalized command name
******** =get-command-completions=
#+begin_src lisp
  (get-command-completions cmd-name text args)
#+end_src

Run the registered completion function for a command.

- =cmd-name= :: Command string such as =\"/add\"=
- =text= :: Current partial token
- =args= :: Already-entered argument list
******** =acp-command-p=
#+begin_src lisp
  (acp-command-p cmd-name)
#+end_src

Return =T= if a command has an ACP handler.
******** =execute-acp-command=
#+begin_src lisp
  (execute-acp-command cmd args)
#+end_src

Execute an ACP handler and return its result alist.
******** =parse-command=
#+begin_src lisp
  (parse-command input)
#+end_src

Parse a command line into either a slash/dot command or a raw prompt.

*Return Value:* Two values:
1. Command name or =NIL=
2. Parsed arguments or raw prompt text
******** =execute-command=
#+begin_src lisp
  (execute-command cmd args)
#+end_src

Execute a slash command or dot command.
******** =command-completer=
#+begin_src lisp
  (command-completer text start end)
#+end_src

Readline completion entry point for commands and command arguments.
******* Macros
******** =define-slash-command=

  (define-slash-command name args &body body)
#+end_src

Define a slash command, optionally with CLI-style option parsing.
******** =define-sub-command=
#+begin_src lisp
  (define-sub-command name args &body body)
#+end_src

Define a CLI subcommand.
******** =define-command=
#+begin_src lisp
  (define-command name args &body body)
#+end_src

Define a command that may register as slash, subcommand, and ACP command.
******** =def-acp-command=

#+end_src

Define an ACP-only command handler.

******* LLM Processing Utilities
******** chunk-for-llm
#+begin_src lisp
  (chunk-for-llm file &key size-of-chunk)
#+end_src

Chunks a file's content into a list of strings based on token limits.
- =file=: Pathname or string representing the file path.
- =size-of-chunk=: (Optional) Token limit for each chunk. Defaults to 50% of the chunking model's context or 2048.

*Return Value:* A list of string chunks, or =NIL= if the file could not be read.
******** process-in-chunks
#+begin_src lisp
  (process-in-chunks chunks prompt)
#+end_src

Process a list of text chunks with the LLM using the given prompt. Uses the model configured in =*chunking-llm*=.
- =chunks=: List of text strings.
- =prompt=: The system prompt to use for processing each chunk.

*Return Value:* A string containing all responses joined by newlines.
******** process-with-llm
#+begin_src lisp
  (process-with-llm file prompt)
#+end_src

Process a file with the LLM by chunking it first.
- =file=: Pathname or string representing the file path.
- =prompt=: The system prompt to use for processing.

*Return Value:* A string containing the joined responses from processing the file chunks.
******** process-docs-with-llm
#+begin_src lisp
  (process-docs-with-llm chunks format-opt output-file)
#+end_src

Process documentation chunks with the LLM to convert or summarize them.
- =chunks=: List of text strings.
- =format-opt=: Target format string (e.g., "markdown", "org").
- =output-file=: (Optional) File path to write the output to.

If =output-file= is provided, writes content to file. Otherwise prints to standard output.

****** prompts.lisp
This file manages the LLM prompt template registry. Prompts are defined as templates (often using mustache format) and registered under keyword names.
******* defprompt
#+begin_src lisp
  (defprompt name &rest args)
#+end_src

Register a prompt template.

- =name=: Keyword or symbol for the prompt name.
- =args=: Optional type as a symbol, followed by property plist or docstring.
  - =:type=: Prompt type symbol (e.g. =system=, =template=, =user=).
  - =:template=: Raw template string.
  - =:file=: Filename of the template (relative to prompts search path).
  - =:system=: System instructions string.
  - =:vars=: List of bound variable names.
  - =:stream=: Boolean indicating if output should be streamed (default =t=).
******* find-prompt
#+begin_src lisp
  (find-prompt name)
#+end_src

Find the prompt struct registered for NAME.
******* get-prompt
#+begin_src lisp
  (get-prompt name &optional file-fallback)
#+end_src

Return the template string registered for NAME. If absent and FILE-FALLBACK is given, load and memoize it from a prompt file.
******* render-prompt
#+begin_src lisp
  (render-prompt name alist &key file-fallback)
#+end_src

Render the prompt NAME via mustache using ALIST bindings.
******* list-prompts
#+begin_src lisp
  (list-prompts)
#+end_src

Return a list of all registered prompt structs sorted by name.
****** context
******* Context Management
These functions control which local files and images are included in the LLM's context window.
******** add-file-to-context
#+begin_src lisp
  (add-file-to-context file-path)
#+end_src

Adds a text file to the context. The content of this file will be included in subsequent prompts sent to the LLM.

- =file-path= (String or Pathname): The path to the text file to add.

The function will warn if adding the file might exceed the current model's token limit.
******** drop-file-from-context
#+begin_src lisp
  (drop-file-from-context file-path)
#+end_src

Removes a text file from the context.

- =file-path= (String or Pathname): The path to the text file to remove.
******** add-image-to-context
#+begin_src lisp
  (add-image-to-context image-path &optional text)
#+end_src

Adds an image to the context for use with vision-capable models.

- =image-path= (String or Pathname): The path to the image file.
- =text= (String, optional): A textual description of the image to
  provide additional context to the LLM.

The function will warn if the image size exceeds the configured limit (=*image-max-size-mb*=). The image is automatically resized and encoded before being sent to the LLM.
******** drop-image-from-context
#+begin_src lisp
  (drop-image-from-context image-path)
#+end_src

Removes an image from the context.

- =image-path= (String or Pathname): The path to the image file to remove.
******** list-context-files
#+begin_src lisp
  (list-context-files)
#+end_src

Prints a list of all text files currently included in the context to standard output.
******* Documentation Context
Hactar can include structured documentation from its internal database in the context.
******** add-doc-to-context
#+begin_src lisp
  (add-doc-to-context doc-plist)
#+end_src

Adds a documentation entry to the context.

- =doc-plist=: A plist representing a single document from the database, typically retrieved via =docs-find=.
******** remove-doc-from-context
#+begin_src lisp
  (remove-doc-from-context doc-id)
#+end_src

Removes a documentation entry from the context by its unique ID.

- =doc-id= (Integer): The ID of the document to remove.
******* Prompt Generation
These functions assemble the final strings that are sent to the LLM.
******** generate-context
#+begin_src lisp
  (generate-context)
#+end_src

The core context generation function. It assembles the full context string by combining:
- The repository map (=*repo-map*=).
- Content of all files in =*files*=, pruned to fit the model's token limit.
- Project stack (=*stack*=), shell (=*shell*=), language (=*language*=), etc.
- Content of all documents in =*docs-context*=.
- Descriptions of all images in =*images*=.

*Return Value:* A single string formatted according to =prompts/context.org=.
******** system-prompt
#+begin_src lisp
  (system-prompt)
#+end_src

Returns the appropriate system prompt string based on the current application mode (=*assistant-mode-active*=). This is the primary function used to get the system prompt for an LLM call.
******** default-system-prompt
#+begin_src lisp
  (default-system-prompt)
#+end_src

Generates the standard system prompt by combining the base template (=system.default.org=) with active rules (=*active-rules*=), the active guide (=*active-guide-file*=), and the general context from =generate-context=.
******** dot-system-prompt
#+begin_src lisp
  (dot-system-prompt)
#+end_src

Generates the specialized system prompt used for handling "dot commands" (e.g., =.cat=, =.ls=). It uses the =system.dot-command.org= template.
******** assistant-mode-system-prompt
#+begin_src lisp
  (assistant-mode-system-prompt)
#+end_src

Generates the system prompt for assistant mode, which is focused on screen analysis and interaction. It uses the =system.assistant.org= template.
******* Guide Management
******** get-active-guide-content
#+begin_src lisp
  (get-active-guide-content)
#+end_src

Reads the content of the currently active guide file (=*active-guide-file*=). It performs size checks and filters out any headlines marked with tags from =*guide-exclude-tags*= (e.g.,
=:nocontext:=).

*Return Value:* A string containing the filtered guide content, or =NIL= on error or if the guide is too large.
******* Utility Functions
******** generate-commit-message
#+begin_src lisp
  (generate-commit-message)
#+end_src

Asks the LLM to generate a single-line Git commit message based on the last two turns of the chat history.

*Return Value:* A string containing the suggested commit message, or =NIL= on failure.
****** db
The =db= functionality in Hactar manages the connection to the SQLite database, which stores documentation, starters, errors, embeddings, and other persistent data. It uses the =sqlite= library and the =sqlite-vec= extension for vector search.
******* Configuration
Database connection parameters are configured via environment variables or globals.

- =*db-path*=: Path to the SQLite database file. (Default: =*hactar-data-path*/hactar.db= or from =$HACTAR_DB_PATH=)
******* Vars and State
- =*connection*= :: The global SQLite connection object.
******* Connection Management
These functions manage the global database connection.
******** connect-db
#+begin_src lisp
  (connect-db)
#+end_src

Establishes a top-level connection to the database using the configured parameters. It also loads the =sqlite-vec= extension. This is typically handled by the application startup.
******** disconnect-db
#+begin_src lisp
  (disconnect-db)
#+end_src

Disconnects the top-level database connection.
******** with-db-connection
#+begin_src lisp
  (with-db-connection &body body)
#+end_src

Ensure a database connection for the dynamic extent of =body=.
******* Database Operations
******** docs-clear-database
#+begin_src lisp
  (docs-clear-database)
#+end_src

Deletes all documents from the =documents= and =vec_documents= tables in the database. This action requires user confirmation via the command line. It also clears the in-memory =*docs-context*= list.
******** errors-clear-database
#+begin_src lisp
  (errors-clear-database)
#+end_src

Deletes all errors from the =errors= and =vec_errors= tables in the database. This action requires user confirmation and also clears the in-memory =*errors-context*= list.
******* Utility Functions
These are internal helper functions for formatting data for SQL queries.
******** format-vector-for-sqlite-vec
#+begin_src lisp
  (format-vector-for-sqlite-vec vector)
#+end_src

Formats a Lisp list of numbers into a JSON string suitable for =sqlite-vec= insertion.

- =vector=: A list of numbers.
******** format-array-for-sqlite
#+begin_src lisp
  (format-array-for-sqlite lisp-list)
#+end_src

Formats a Lisp list of strings into a JSON array string for SQLite.

- =lisp-list=: A list of strings.
****** rag
RAG handling stuff is rag.lisp.
******* Document Creation
******** docs-create
#+begin_src lisp
  (docs-create &key source title content (tags #()) (covers #()) (links_to #()) slug type meta)
#+end_src

Creates one or more document entries in the database. It automatically handles content splitting for large documents and generates vector embeddings for searching (using =sqlite-vec=). If a document with the same =source= already exists, it will be replaced.

- =&key=:
  - =source= (String, required): The origin of the document (e.g., a URL
    or file path). This is used as a unique identifier for the content.
  - =title= (String, required): The title of the document.
  - =content= (String, required): The textual content of the document.
  - =tags= (List of Strings, optional): A list of tags for
    categorization (e.g., =("api", "react")=).
  - =covers= (List of Strings, optional): A list of technologies or
    topics this document covers (e.g., =("react@18", "typescript")=).
  - =links_to= (List of Strings, optional): A list of other document IDs
    this document references.
  - =slug= (String, optional): A URL-friendly slug for the document.
  - =type= (String, optional): The type of document (e.g.,
    "documentation", "example").
  - =meta= (Plist or Alist, optional): A plist or alist of arbitrary
    metadata to be stored as a JSON object.

*Return Value:* A list of integer IDs for the newly created document entries.
******* Document Retrieval
******** docs-find
#+begin_src lisp
  (docs-find &key tags covers slug sources text type id (limit 10) (offset 0) (match-any nil))
#+end_src

Finds documents in the database based on a combination of metadata filters and semantic text search (using =sqlite-vec=).

- =&key=:
  - =text= (String, optional): If provided, performs a vector similarity
    search on the document content. Results are ordered by relevance.
  - =tags= (List of Strings, optional): Filters for documents that
    contain *all* of the specified tags (or ANY if match-any is T).
  - =covers= (List of Strings, optional): Filters for documents that
    cover *all* of the specified topics (or ANY if match-any is T).
  - =sources= (List of Strings, optional): Filters for documents that
    match *any* of the specified source strings.
  - =id= (Integer, optional): Finds a document by its exact unique ID.
  - =slug= (String, optional): Finds a document by its exact slug.
  - =type= (String, optional): Finds documents by their exact type.
  - =limit= (Integer, optional): The maximum number of documents to
    return (Default: 10).
  - =offset= (Integer, optional): The number of results to skip (for
    pagination).
  - =match-any= (Boolean, optional): If T, tags and covers use OR logic instead of AND
    .

*Return Value:* A list of plists, where each plist represents a document matching the search criteria. The document plist contains keys like =:id=, =:title=, =:content=, =:tags=, =:covers=, =:source=, etc.
******** starters-find
#+begin_src lisp
  (starters-find &rest args &key tags &allow-other-keys)
#+end_src

A convenience wrapper around =docs-find= that automatically adds the ="starter"= tag to the search query. It accepts all the same arguments as =docs-find=.
****** tui
Hactar uses a bunch of different TUI stuff. Where possible we wrap command CLI tools like FZF, and where not we hand roll our own
******* High-Level Components
The primary functions for creating interactive selections and prompts.
******** select-with-fzf
#+begin_src lisp
  (select-with-fzf items &key preview-command)
#+end_src

Presents a list of items to the user for selection using the external =fzf= command-line tool. This function requires =fzf= to be installed and available in the system's =PATH=.

- =items= (List of Strings): The list of strings to be displayed for
  selection.
- =&key=:
  - =preview-command= (String, optional):
    A shell command string to be used by =fzf= for generating a preview for the highlighted item. The placeholder ={}= can be used in the command to represent the selected item.

*Return Value:* The string of the selected item, or =NIL= if the user cancels the selection (e.g., by pressing =Esc= or =Ctrl-C=).
******** select-doc-with-fzf
#+begin_src lisp
  (select-doc-with-fzf doc-list)
#+end_src

A specialized version of =select-with-fzf= designed for selecting from a list of documentation plists. It displays the document title for selection and a formatted preview of the full document.

- =doc-list= (List of Plists): A list of document plists, as returned by
  =docs-find=. Each plist must contain at least an =:id= and a =:title=.

*Return Value:* The full plist of the selected document, or =NIL= if the selection is cancelled.
******** confirm-action
#+begin_src lisp
  (confirm-action prompt)
#+end_src

Prompts the user with a "Yes/No" question and waits for their input.

- =prompt= (String): The question to display to the user (e.g., "Are you
  sure?").

*Return Value:*
- =T= if the user enters "y" or "Y".
- =NIL= if the user enters "n" or "N".
- The function will re-prompt if any other input is given.
******** get-multiline-input
#+begin_src lisp
  (get-multiline-input)
#+end_src

Opens the user's default editor (=$EDITOR=, falling back to =nano=) to allow for multi-line text input. This is useful for writing long prompts or messages.

*Return Value:* A string containing the text entered by the user. Lines starting with =#= are treated as comments and are removed from the final string.
******* Low-Level TUI (Internal)
The following function provides an in-Lisp TUI selector, which is used as a fallback or for environments where =fzf= is not available. It is not typically called directly.
******** fuzzy-select
#+begin_src lisp
  (fuzzy-select items)
#+end_src

Displays a TUI selector built within Common Lisp, without external dependencies. It provides a two-pane view with a filterable list on the left and a preview on the right.

- =items= (List of Plists):
  A list where each element is a plist containing at least =(:item . "display-string")= and =(:preview . "preview-text")=.

*Return Value:* The full plist of the selected item, or =NIL= if the selection is cancelled.
****** interface.lisp
This component implements a two-way file interface system that maps the internal application state to temporary files under a unique instance directory (e.g. =./.hactar/<pid>/=). Edits to these files by the user (or external editors) are automatically synchronized back into Hactar's state, and state changes are written out to the files.
******* definterface
#+begin_src lisp
  (definterface name path &key (format :text) render parse on-change hooks (watch t) sections title)
#+end_src

Define a two-way file interface NAME mapped to PATH under the instance dir.

- =name=: Keyword identifier for the interface (e.g. =:files=, =:state=).
- =path=: Relative path string under the instance directory.
- =format=: Format keyword (=:text=, =:org=, =:lisp=).
- =render=: Parameterless lambda returning a string to write to the file.
- =parse=: Lambda taking the file content string and applying it to the application state.
- =on-change=: Alternate fallback function to call when the file is modified (if parse is absent).
- =hooks=: List of =(hook-variable direction)= pairs (where direction is =:in= or =:out=) to trigger syncs.
- =watch=: If true (default), installs a file watcher to detect external changes.
- =sections=: List of plists for =:org= format files to parse sections into separate handlers.
- =title=: Optional title for the top of org files.
******* instance-id
#+begin_src lisp
  (instance-id)
#+end_src

Return and memoize the unique instance ID string (typically the PID).
******* instance-dir
#+begin_src lisp
  (instance-dir)
#+end_src

Return and ensure the absolute pathname of Hactar's temporary instance directory.
******* interface-abs-path
#+begin_src lisp
  (interface-abs-path iface)
#+end_src

Return the absolute pathname of the given interface struct's file.
******* materialize-interface
#+begin_src lisp
  (materialize-interface iface)
#+end_src

Write the initial file for IFACE and install its watcher and declared hooks.
******* materialize-all-interfaces
#+begin_src lisp
  (materialize-all-interfaces)
#+end_src

Materialize all registered interfaces into the instance directory.
******* sync-interface-out
#+begin_src lisp
  (sync-interface-out name)
#+end_src

Re-render and write the named interface file.
******* sync-interface-in
#+begin_src lisp
  (sync-interface-in name)
#+end_src

Read the named interface file and apply its content to the application state.
******* with-interface-suppressed
#+begin_src lisp
  (with-interface-suppressed (name) &body body)
#+end_src

Run body, then update the interface's hash to ignore filesystem changes caused by Hactar itself during the body's execution.
****** import.lisp
This file provides a system for importing documentation from various external sources. It uses a registry of "import sources" that match against a URI using regular expressions. This is similar to the `router.lisp` file but is specifically designed for fetching, processing, and ingesting new content into the document database.

When a URI is provided (e.g., "npm:react@latest", =file:~/notes.md=, "https://github.com/user/repo"), this system finds a matching source, executes its handler to retrieve the content, automatically generates metadata (tags and summary) using an LLM, and then creates a new document.
******* variables
******** import-sources
#+begin_src lisp
  (defvar *import-sources* (make-hash-table :test 'equal))
#+end_src
This global hash table is the central registry for all defined import sources. It maps a source name (a symbol, e.g., `npm-source`) to its corresponding `import-source` struct instance.
******* structs
******** import-source
#+begin_src lisp
  (defstruct import-source
    name        ; Source name (symbol)
    pattern     ; Regex pattern string
    param-names ; List of parameter names to extract from regex groups
    priority    ; Integer priority (higher = checked first)
    handler)    ; Function that retrieves content (package version) -> (values content title)
#+end_src
This structure defines a single import provider.
- ~name~: A unique symbol identifying the source.
- ~pattern~: A CL-PPCRE compatible regular expression string used to match against an input URI.
- ~param-names~: A list of symbols that correspond *in order* to the capture groups in the ~pattern~.
- ~priority~: An integer. Sources with higher priority numbers are checked before sources with lower numbers.
- ~handler~: A function that performs the import. It receives the extracted parameters as arguments and *must* return two values: the fetched ~content~ (as a string) and a ~title~ (as a string).
******* functions
******** register-import-source
#+begin_src lisp
  (defun register-import-source (name pattern param-names priority handler))
#+end_src
This is the low-level function for manually adding a new import source to the `*import-sources*` registry. It instantiates an `import-source` struct and saves it. The `defsource` macro is the preferred, high-level way to define a source.
********* Example
#+begin_src lisp
  ;; Manually register a source for local wiki files
  (register-import-source 'local-wiki-source
                          "^wiki:(.+)$"
                          '(:page-name)
                          10
                          (lambda (page-name)
                            (let ((path (format nil "/var/wiki/~A.md" page-name)))
                              (values (uiop:read-file-string path)
                                      page-name))))
#+end_src
******** match-import-source
#+begin_src lisp
  (defun match-import-source (uri))
#+end_src
This function attempts to find a matching `import-source` for the given `uri` string. It collects all sources from the `*import-sources*` table, sorts them by priority (highest first), and iterates through them. The first source whose `pattern` matches the `uri` is selected.

It returns two values: the matching `import-source` struct and an alist of `(param-name . value)` pairs. If no source matches, it returns `(values nil nil)`.
********* Example
#+begin_src lisp
  (multiple-value-bind (source params)
      (match-import-source "wiki:Main_Page")
    (when source
      (format t "Matched source: ~A~%" (import-source-name source))
      (format t "Params: ~A~%" params)))

  ;; Output:
  ;; Matched source: LOCAL-WIKI-SOURCE
  ;; Params: ((:PAGE-NAME . "Main_Page"))
#+end_src
******** generate-doc-metadata
#+begin_src lisp
  (defun generate-doc-metadata (content title source-uri))
#+end_src
This utility function uses an LLM to automatically generate metadata for new content. It sends the ~content~, ~title~, and ~source-uri~ to the LLM with a prompt requesting a comma-separated list of tags and a one-line summary. It then parses the LLM's plain text response to extract these two pieces of data.

It returns two values: a list of string tags and a single summary string.
******** execute-import
#+begin_src lisp
  (defun execute-import (uri &key tags covers meta))
#+end_src
This is the main, high-level function for running the entire import process. It takes a `uri` and optional, manually-provided metadata.

Its workflow is as follows:
1. It calls `match-import-source` with the `uri`.
2. If a source is found, it executes the source's `handler` with the extracted parameters to get the `content` and `title`.
3. If `tags` were *not* provided as a keyword argument, it calls `generate-doc-metadata` to create them automatically.
4. It then calls `docs-create` to save the content, title, and all metadata to the document database.
5. It prints a status message to standard output.

If no source matches the `uri`, or if the handler fails, it prints an error message and returns `nil`. On success, it returns the ID(s) of the newly created document(s).
********* Example
#+begin_src lisp
  ;; Import a document and let the LLM generate metadata
  (execute-import "npm:react@19.0.0")

  ;; Import a local file and provide manual metadata
  (execute-import "file:~/my-notes.md"
                  :tags '("personal" "project-alpha")
                  :covers '("notes-alpha"))
#+end_src
******** docs-import-common
#+begin_src lisp
  (defun %docs-import-common (args &key extra-tags usage))
#+end_src
This is a private helper function used by the CLI commands (`/import`, `/import.starter`, etc.). It handles the common logic of parsing the command arguments, separating the `uri` from the metadata key/value pairs (like `:tags`, `:covers`), and merging any `extra-tags` (e.g., adding "starter") before finally calling `execute-import`.
******* macros
******** defsource
#+begin_src lisp
  (defmacro defsource (name &rest args))
#+end_src
This is the primary, declarative macro for defining a new import source. It is a user-friendly wrapper around `register-import-source` that handles parsing keyword arguments and constructing the handler lambda.

- ~name~: The symbol to name this source (e.g., `npm-source`).
- ~:pattern~: The regex string to match URIs.
- ~:params~: A list of symbols for the regex capture groups. These become the lambda list for the handler body.
- ~:priority~: (Optional) An integer priority (default 10).
- ~body~: The Lisp forms to execute as the handler. This code *must* return two values: `(values content title)`.
********* Example
#+begin_src lisp
  ;; Define a source for importing from a specific GitHub repo's "docs" folder
  (defsource my-project-docs
    :pattern "^my-project:(.+)$"
    :params (:doc-name)
    :priority 20
    (let* ((url (format nil "https://raw.githubusercontent.com/user/my-project/main/docs/~A.md" doc-name))
           (content (fetch-url-content url)))
      (values content (format nil "My Project: ~A" doc-name))))

  ;; This can now be imported
  ;; (execute-import "my-project:installation")
#+end_src
******** defdocsource
#+begin_src lisp
  (defmacro defdocsource (&key name version platform uri))
#+end_src
This macro is a specialized helper that *does not* define an import source. Instead, it defines a *custom documentation route* using `defroute` (from `router.lisp`).

This is used to *override* the default behavior of another import source. For example, the built-in `npm-source` calls `get-npm-docs`, which in turn calls `execute-route`. `defdoc` injects a high-priority route that `execute-route` will find first, allowing you to point a specific package/version (e.g., "react@19.^") to a specific static `uri` (like a README on a specific branch) instead of letting `npm-source` try to find it dynamically.
********* Example
#+begin_src lisp
  ;; This route will be matched by the router,
  ;; effectively overriding the default 'get-npm-docs' logic
  ;; for React 19.
  (defdocsourc :name "react"
          :version "19.^"
          :platform "npm"
          :uri "https://raw.githubusercontent.com/facebook/react/main/README.md")
#+end_src
******* Built-in Import Sources
The file defines several sources by default using `defsource`:

- **npm-source**:
  - *Pattern*: `"^npm:([^@]+)@(.+)$"`
  - *Description*: Imports documentation for an NPM package by calling `get-npm-docs`.
- **file-source**:
  - *Pattern*: `"^file:(.+)$"`
  - *Description*: Imports a local file. The path is resolved relative to `*repo-root*`.
- **http-source**:
  - *Pattern*: `"^https?://(.+)$"`
  - *Description*: A low-priority (5) fallback that fetches content from any `http` or `https` URL.
- **github-repo-source**:
  - *Pattern*: `"^https?://github\\.com/([^/]+)/([^/]+)/?$"`
  - *Description*: A high-priority (15) source that specifically matches GitHub repository URLs and fetches their main `README.md` file.
******* Commands
This file also defines several user-facing chat commands for triggering the import process.
******** /import
#+begin_src lisp
  (define-command import (args))
#+end_src
The primary command for importing documentation.
- *Usage*: `/import <uri> -tags=tag1 -covers=cover1`
- *Example*: `/import npm:react@latest -tags=framework,ui`
******** /docs-import (and /import.docs)
#+begin_src lisp
  (define-command docs-import (args))
  (define-command import.docs (args))
#+end_src
Aliases for the `/import` command with identical functionality.
******** /import.starter
#+begin_src lisp
  (define-command import.starter (args))
#+end_src
A specialized version of `/import` that automatically adds the `"starter"` tag to any document it imports, in addition to any tags provided manually or generated by the LLM.
****** mode.lisp
This file implements the Hactar "mode" system. Modes are bundles of features, commands, and rules that can be activated dynamically when stack criteria are met (e.g. React project structure detected) or manually by the user.
******* defmode
#+begin_src lisp
  (defmode name description &body body)
#+end_src

Define a mode.

- =name=: Symbol or string identifying the mode.
- =description=: Docstring description.
- =body=: Property plist with keys:
  - =:when=: Form/predicate that returns true if the mode should be automatically activated.
  - =:rules=: Rule text to add to the system prompt when active.
  - =:skills=: List of skills to load when active.
  - =:commands=: List of mode-specific command definitions.
  - =:on-activate=: Function to run upon activation.
  - =:on-deactivate=: Function to run upon deactivation.
******* defmode-command
#+begin_src lisp
  (defmode-command mode name args &body body)
#+end_src

Define a command namespaced under MODE that only runs when the mode is active. The command name is registered globally as =mode.name=.
******* get-mode
#+begin_src lisp
  (get-mode name)
#+end_src

Look up a registered mode struct by name.
******* activate-mode
#+begin_src lisp
  (activate-mode name)
#+end_src

Activate a mode, injecting its rules, loading its skills, loading stack documentation, and calling its =on-activate= callback.
******* deactivate-mode
#+begin_src lisp
  (deactivate-mode name)
#+end_src

Deactivate a mode, removing its rules and calling its =on-deactivate= callback.
******* active-modes
#+begin_src lisp
  (active-modes)
#+end_src

Return a list of all currently active mode names.
******* refresh-modes
#+begin_src lisp
  (refresh-modes)
#+end_src

Re-evaluate the =:when= predicates of all modes, activating or deactivating them as necessary.
******* get-active-mode-rules
#+begin_src lisp
  (get-active-mode-rules)
#+end_src

Collect active mode rules into a single formatted string for insertion into the LLM system prompt.
****** hactar-monolith
The =hactar-monolith= component transforms Hactar into an Org-Centric Literate Programming Mode, where org-mode files become the source of truth for all code and concepts. It manages a knowledge graph of concepts, projects, and journal entries.
******* Core Functions
******** init-monolith
#+begin_src lisp
  (init-monolith path)
#+end_src

Initialize a new knowledge monolith at =PATH=. Creates the directory structure and SQLite database.
******** index-monolith
#+begin_src lisp
  (index-monolith &key force)
#+end_src

Index the entire knowledge monolith, parsing org files and updating the database.
******* Concept Operations
******** create-concept
#+begin_src lisp
  (create-concept title &key maturity languages content path)
#+end_src

Create a new concept org file and index it.
******** find-concepts
#+begin_src lisp
  (find-concepts query &key maturity language limit)
#+end_src

Find concepts matching a query string, optionally filtering by maturity or language.
******** get-concept
#+begin_src lisp
  (get-concept id)
#+end_src

Get a concept by its ID.
******** update-concept-maturity
#+begin_src lisp
  (update-concept-maturity id new-maturity)
#+end_src

Update a concept's maturity level in both the database and the org file.
******* Tangling & Drift
******** tangle-project
#+begin_src lisp
  (tangle-project project-name &key dry-run lang)
#+end_src

Tangle all code blocks for a specific project.
******** tangle-file
#+begin_src lisp
  (tangle-file file-path &key dry-run)
#+end_src

Tangle code blocks from a single org file.
******** detect-drift
#+begin_src lisp
  (detect-drift &key project all)
#+end_src

Detect drift between org source blocks and tangled files.
******* Graph Queries
******** get-related-concepts
#+begin_src lisp
  (get-related-concepts id &key relation depth)
#+end_src

Get concepts related to the given ID up to a certain depth.
******** query-graph
#+begin_src lisp
  (query-graph query-string)
#+end_src

Execute a natural language query against the knowledge graph.
******* Commands
- =/monolith-init [path]=: Initialize a new knowledge monolith.
- =/monolith-status=: Show status of the knowledge monolith.
- =/monolith-index [--force]=: Index the knowledge monolith.
- =/concept-new <title> [--maturity <level>] [--lang <languages>]=: Create a new concept.
- =/concept-find <query> [--maturity <level>] [--lang <language>]=: Find concepts.
- =/concept-mature <id-or-title> --to <maturity>=: Promote a concept to a higher maturity level.
- =/tangle --project <name> [--lang <language>] [--dry-run]=: Extract code from org files for a project.
- =/tangle --file <path> [--dry-run]=: Extract code from a specific org file.
- =/drift --project <name> | --all=: Detect drift between org and tangled code.
- =/graph-query <natural language query>=: Query the knowledge graph.
- =/remember <thought> [--link-to <concept>]=: Quick capture of ideas with auto-linking.
- =/synthesize <description> --draw-from <glob patterns>=: Generate new code by composing existing concepts.
- =/agent <name> <task>=: Interact with a monolith agent (librarian, architect, implementer, critic).

CLI Sub-commands:
- =hactar monolith.init [path]=
- =hactar monolith.index [--force]=
- =hactar monolith.tangle --project <name> [--lang <language>] [--dry-run]=
- =hactar monolith.drift [--project <name>] [--all]=
- =hactar monolith.concept <new|find|list> [args]=
- =hactar monolith.synthesize <description> --draw-from <patterns...>=
****** wiki.lisp
This file implements the Hactar Wiki knowledge graph. It provides a structured registry of docsets, endpoints, components, and variables that form a semantic network. Unknown URIs can trigger automated LLM queries that fall back to search and synthesis against this graph.
******* defdocset
#+begin_src lisp
  (defdocset name &key version stack-tags description)
#+end_src

Declare a docset namespace. Subsequent defendpoint/defcomponent/defvariable calls in this file inherit its STACK-TAGS unless overridden.
******* defendpoint
#+begin_src lisp
  (defendpoint qualified-name &rest props)
#+end_src

Define a wiki endpoint node. QUALIFIED-NAME should be formatted as =docset/endpoint-path=.
******* defcomponent
#+begin_src lisp
  (defcomponent qualified-name &rest props)
#+end_src

Define a wiki component node (e.g. UI component). QUALIFIED-NAME should be formatted as =docset/component-path=.
******* defvariable
#+begin_src lisp
  (defvariable qualified-name &rest props)
#+end_src

Define a wiki variable or configuration node. QUALIFIED-NAME should be formatted as =docset/variable-path=.
******* defimporter
#+begin_src lisp
  (defimporter name (&rest lambda-list) &body body)
#+end_src

Define a wiki importer named NAME that processes external documents and emits Lisp registry forms.
******* parse-wiki-uri
#+begin_src lisp
  (parse-wiki-uri uri-string)
#+end_src

Parse a wiki URI string into three values: (values namespace path resource).
******* find-wiki-node
#+begin_src lisp
  (find-wiki-node namespace path)
#+end_src

Find a registered wiki node. If NAMESPACE is nil, tries to infer it from the active =*stack*=.
******* dispatch-wiki-query
#+begin_src lisp
  (dispatch-wiki-query uri-string)
#+end_src

Main entry point for resolving wiki requests. Parses the URI, looks up the corresponding node, and returns the requested resource property or synthesizes it with an LLM.
******* wiki-import
#+begin_src lisp
  (wiki-import importer-name &rest args)
#+end_src

Invoke the named importer with the provided arguments.
******* wiki-list
#+begin_src lisp
  (wiki-list &optional namespace-filter)
#+end_src

Print all registered wiki nodes, optionally filtered by namespace prefix.
******* wiki-show
#+begin_src lisp
  (wiki-show uri)
#+end_src

Display the properties and relationships of a single wiki node.
****** litmode
The =litmode= component implements Single-File Literate Mode for Hactar. A single =.hactar.org= file per project becomes the sole interface between a human and Hactar. All context engineering, code changes, scripting, and agent coordination flows through this one file.
******* Core Functions
******** init-litmode
#+begin_src lisp
  (init-litmode &optional path)
#+end_src

Initialize literate single-file mode. Creates a default =.hactar.org= file if it doesn't exist, initializes the SQLite database, and builds the initial headline index.

- =path=: Directory or explicit =.hactar.org= path. Defaults to =*repo-root*=.
******** litmode-active-p
#+begin_src lisp
  (litmode-active-p)
#+end_src

Return =T= if literate mode is currently active.
******** load-litmode-file
#+begin_src lisp
  (load-litmode-file &optional force)
#+end_src

Load and parse the =.hactar.org= file. Uses cache unless =force= is =T=.
******** save-litmode-file
#+begin_src lisp
  (save-litmode-file &optional doc)
#+end_src

Serialize and write the current parsed document back to the =.hactar.org= file.
******* Context & Scope Management
******** set-active-scope
#+begin_src lisp
  (set-active-scope scope-name)
#+end_src

Set the active scope profile. Clears expand/focus state when scope changes.
******** get-active-scope
#+begin_src lisp
  (get-active-scope)
#+end_src

Return the currently active scope name.
******** expand-context
#+begin_src lisp
  (expand-context headline-ids &optional reason)
#+end_src

Expand context to include additional headline IDs.
******** focus-context
#+begin_src lisp
  (focus-context headline-id &optional reason)
#+end_src

Focus context on a single headline (plus pins and index).
******** generate-litmode-context
#+begin_src lisp
  (generate-litmode-context)
#+end_src

Generate the context string from the =.hactar.org= file based on current scope. This replaces the normal context generation when litmode is active.
******* Tangling & Untangling
******** tangle-code-zone
#+begin_src lisp
  (tangle-code-zone &key dry-run)
#+end_src

Tangle all code blocks from the Code zone to their target files. Returns a list of written file paths.
******** tangle-block
#+begin_src lisp
  (tangle-block heading-id &key dry-run)
#+end_src

Tangle a single code block by its heading ID.
******** untangle-file
#+begin_src lisp
  (untangle-file file-path)
#+end_src

Pull changes from a tangled file back into the =.hactar.org= source.
******** detect-litmode-drift
#+begin_src lisp
  (detect-litmode-drift)
#+end_src

Detect drift between org source blocks and tangled files. Returns a list of drift plists.
******* Task & Lock Management
******** get-tasks
#+begin_src lisp
  (get-tasks &key state)
#+end_src

Get tasks from the Tasks zone. Optionally filter by =state= (TODO, DOING, DONE, BLOCKED).
******** transition-task
#+begin_src lisp
  (transition-task task-id new-state)
#+end_src

Transition a task to a new state. Handles state transitions like activating scope and acquiring/releasing locks.
******** acquire-lock
#+begin_src lisp
  (acquire-lock headline-ids &key scope-name)
#+end_src

Acquire locks on the given headline IDs for this agent. Returns =T= on success, =NIL= on conflict.
******** release-lock
#+begin_src lisp
  (release-lock headline-ids)
#+end_src

Release locks on the given headline IDs for this agent.
******* Scripting & Tools
******** register-org-tools
#+begin_src lisp
  (register-org-tools)
#+end_src

Scan the Tooling section and register named src blocks.
******** run-named-block
#+begin_src lisp
  (run-named-block name)
#+end_src

Execute a named src block. Supports shell commands and Lisp code.
******* Commands
- =/litmode-init [path]=: Initialize literate single-file mode.
- =/scope [name] | --list=: Set or show the active scope profile.
- =/expand <id1> [id2 ...]=: Expand context to include additional headlines.
- =/focus <id> | --clear=: Focus context on a single headline.
- =/litmode-index=: Rebuild the headline index.
- =/litmode-tangle [--dry-run] | <heading-id>=: Tangle code from =.hactar.org= to files.
- =/litmode-untangle <file-path>=: Pull changes from tangled files back into =.hactar.org=.
- =/litmode-drift=: Detect drift between org source and tangled files.
- =/litmode-tasks [--state <TODO|DOING|DONE|BLOCKED>]=: Show tasks from =.hactar.org=.
- =/litmode-task-do <task-id> <state>=: Transition a task to a new state.
- =/litmode-locks [--cleanup]=: Show active agent locks.
- =/run <name>=: Run a named src block from the Tooling section.
- =/litmode-summarize=: Auto-generate summaries for headlines without one.
- =/litmode-status=: Show literate mode status.
****** vfs
=vfs.lisp= Holds a virtual filesystem. This is used so stuff like create commands and compiler targets can generate any filesystem structure in one pass.
******* Data Structures
******** =vfs=
A virtual file system that tracks files and the current output file.
******** =vfs-file=
A single virtual file with path, content buffer, and metadata.
******* Core Functions
******** =vfs-select-file=
#+begin_src lisp
  (vfs-select-file vfs path)
#+end_src

Select or create the current file.
******** =vfs-current-vfs-file=
#+begin_src lisp
  (vfs-current-vfs-file vfs)
#+end_src

Return the currently selected VFS file.
******** =vfs-write=
#+begin_src lisp
  (vfs-write vfs string)
#+end_src

Append text to the current file.
******** =vfs-prepend=
#+begin_src lisp
  (vfs-prepend vfs string)
#+end_src

Prepend text to the current file.
******** =vfs-writeln=
#+begin_src lisp
  (vfs-writeln vfs string)
#+end_src

Append text and newline.
******** =vfs-get-content=
#+begin_src lisp
  (vfs-get-content vfs path)
#+end_src

Return file contents as a string.
******** =vfs-all-paths=
#+begin_src lisp
  (vfs-all-paths vfs)
#+end_src

Return all VFS file paths.
******** =vfs-flush-to-disk=
#+begin_src lisp
  (vfs-flush-to-disk vfs output-root)
#+end_src

Write all VFS files to disk.
******** =vfs-flush-to-org=
#+begin_src lisp
  (vfs-flush-to-org vfs &optional (stream *standard-output*) (tangle-dir "."))
#+end_src

Emit all VFS files as Org tangled blocks.
******** =vfs-flush-to-lisp=
#+begin_src lisp
  (vfs-flush-to-lisp vfs &optional (stream *standard-output*))
#+end_src

Emit Lisp code to reconstruct the VFS.
******** =vfs-flush-to-tags=
#+begin_src lisp
  (vfs-flush-to-tags vfs &optional (stream *standard-output*))
#+end_src

Emit all VFS files in =<file>= tag format.
******** =vfs-set-metadata=
#+begin_src lisp
  (vfs-set-metadata vfs path key value)
#+end_src

Set metadata on a VFS file.
******** =vfs-get-metadata=
#+begin_src lisp
  (vfs-get-metadata vfs path key)
#+end_src

Get metadata from a VFS file.
****** compiler targets
Hactar includes a language-target compiler layer for generating source files from Lisp forms. These targets are especially useful for starter kits, code generators, literate workflows, and deterministic scaffolding.
******* javascript target
The =javascript-target.lisp= component defines the core JS emitter layer.

Key capabilities include:
- function and variable emission
- conditionals and boolean operators
- object and array literals
- imports and exports
- async/await
- JSX-adjacent support consumed by higher-level targets
******** Helper Functions
********* =emit-name=
#+begin_src lisp
  (emit-name symbol)
#+end_src

Emit a Lisp symbol as a JavaScript identifier.
********* =emit-atom=
#+begin_src lisp
  (emit-atom atom)
#+end_src

Emit an atom as JavaScript.
********* =emit-funcall=
#+begin_src lisp
  (emit-funcall op args)
#+end_src

Emit a generic function call.
********* =emit-separated=
#+begin_src lisp
  (emit-separated separator forms)
#+end_src

Emit forms separated by a delimiter.
********* =emit-block=
#+begin_src lisp
  (emit-block body)
#+end_src

Emit a JavaScript block with indentation.
********* =emit-js-arg=
#+begin_src lisp
  (emit-js-arg arg)
#+end_src

Emit a JavaScript function argument, including destructuring support.
********* =js-statement-p=
#+begin_src lisp
  (js-statement-p form)
#+end_src

Return =T= if a form compiles to a statement form.
******** Key Forms
********* =defun=
#+begin_src lisp
  (defun name args &body body)
#+end_src

Emit a JavaScript function declaration.
********* =defvar=
#+begin_src lisp
  (defvar name &optional value)
#+end_src

Emit a =var= declaration.
********* =defconst=
#+begin_src lisp
  (defconst name &optional value)
#+end_src

Emit a =const= declaration.
********* =let=
#+begin_src lisp
  (let (bindings) &body body)
#+end_src

Emit JavaScript =let= bindings.
********* =let*=
#+begin_src lisp
  (let* (bindings) &body body)
#+end_src

Emit JavaScript =const= bindings.
********* =setf=
#+begin_src lisp
  (setf place value)
#+end_src

Emit assignment.
********* =if=
#+begin_src lisp
  (if condition then &optional else)
#+end_src

Emit an =if/else= statement.
********* =cond=
#+begin_src lisp
  (cond &rest clauses)
#+end_src

Emit chained conditional logic.
********* =lambda=
#+begin_src lisp
  (lambda args &body body)
#+end_src

Emit an arrow function.
********* =async=
#+begin_src lisp
  (async form)
#+end_src

Emit =async= form.
********* =await=
#+begin_src lisp
  (await form)
#+end_src

Emit =await= form.
********* =return=
#+begin_src lisp
  (return form)
#+end_src

Emit a return statement.
********* =@=
#+begin_src lisp
  (@ obj &rest keys)
#+end_src

Emit chained property access.
********* =create=
#+begin_src lisp
  (create &rest pairs)
#+end_src

Emit an object literal.
********* =array=
#+begin_src lisp
  (array &rest elements)
#+end_src

Emit an array literal.
********* =try=
#+begin_src lisp
  (try &rest forms)
#+end_src

Emit a =try/catch= block.
********* =throw=
#+begin_src lisp
  (throw form)
#+end_src

Emit a throw statement.
********* =export=
#+begin_src lisp
  (export form)
#+end_src

Emit an export statement.
********* =export-default=
#+begin_src lisp
  (export-default form)
#+end_src

Emit an export default statement.
********* =import=
#+begin_src lisp
  (import what &key from)
#+end_src

Emit static or dynamic imports.
********* =comment=
#+begin_src lisp
  (comment text)
#+end_src

Emit a single-line comment.
********* =in-file=
#+begin_src lisp
  (in-file path)
#+end_src

Switch the active VFS file.
********* =destructuring-const=
#+begin_src lisp
  (destructuring-const vars expr)
#+end_src

Emit destructuring assignment with =const=.
********* =progn=
#+begin_src lisp
  (progn &rest forms)
#+end_src

Emit multiple forms sequentially.
********* =template=
#+begin_src lisp
  (template &rest parts)
#+end_src

Emit a template literal.
********* =|?:|=
#+begin_src lisp
  (|?:| condition then else)
#+end_src

Emit a ternary expression.
********* =chain=
#+begin_src lisp
  (chain obj &rest calls)
#+end_src

Emit chained method calls.
********* =json-stringify=
#+begin_src lisp
  (json-stringify data)
#+end_src

Emit =JSON.stringify(...)=.
********* =json-parse=
#+begin_src lisp
  (json-parse data)
#+end_src

Emit =JSON.parse(...)=.
******** Convenience Macros
********* =when=
#+begin_src lisp
  (when condition &rest body)
#+end_src

Expand to a one-branch =if=.
********* =unless=
#+begin_src lisp
  (unless condition &rest body)
#+end_src

Expand to a negated =if=.
********* =map=
#+begin_src lisp
  (map arr fn)
#+end_src

Expand to =arr.map(fn)=.
********* =filter=
#+begin_src lisp
  (filter arr fn)
#+end_src

Expand to =arr.filter(fn)=.
********* =reduce=
#+begin_src lisp
  (reduce arr fn &optional initial)
#+end_src

Expand to =arr.reduce(...)=.  
******* typescript target
The =typescript-target.lisp= component extends the JavaScript target with type-aware emitters.

Key capabilities include:
- typed function arguments
- optional return type support
- typed let/const bindings
- typed lambdas
- =const-typed= helper emission
******** Helper Functions
********* =extract-type-annotation=
#+begin_src lisp
  (extract-type-annotation arg-form)
#+end_src

Parse typed argument forms and return normalized name and type string.
******** Key Forms
********* =defun=
#+begin_src lisp
  (defun name args &body body)
#+end_src

Emit a typed TypeScript function declaration.
********* =let=
#+begin_src lisp
  (let (bindings) &body body)
#+end_src

Emit typed =let= bindings.
********* =let*=
#+begin_src lisp
  (let* (bindings) &body body)
#+end_src

Emit typed =const= bindings.
********* =lambda=
#+begin_src lisp
  (lambda args &body body)
#+end_src

Emit an arrow function with typed parameters.
********* =const-typed=
#+begin_src lisp
  (const-typed name type-str value)
#+end_src

Emit =const name: Type = value=.
******* worker target
The =worker-target.lisp= component targets Cloudflare Worker-style modules.

Key capabilities include:
- =defworker= emitter for =export default { async fetch(...) { ... } }=
- =json-response= macro
- =text-response= macro
- worker-style =fetch= emission with option object handling

#+end_src

#+end_src

Emit a JSON Cloudflare =Response=.
********* =text-response=
#+begin_src lisp
  (text-response data &key (status 200))
#+end_src

Emit a text Cloudflare =Response=.

******* css target
The =css-target.lisp= component emits CSS and supports a nested DSL for selectors and declarations.

Key forms include:
- =css-decl=
- =css-rule=
- =css-nested-rule=
- =css-at-rule=
- =css-stylesheet=
- =defcss=
******** Helper Functions
********* =css-selector-from-form=
#+begin_src lisp
  (css-selector-from-form selector)
#+end_src

Normalize a selector form into CSS selector text.
********* =css-property-name=
#+begin_src lisp
  (css-property-name property)
#+end_src

Normalize a CSS property keyword.
********* =css-at-rule-p=
#+begin_src lisp
  (css-at-rule-p selector)
#+end_src

Return =T= if selector is an at-rule.
********* =css-combine-selectors=
#+begin_src lisp
  (css-combine-selectors parent child)
#+end_src

Combine nested selectors.
********* =css-property-unitless-p=
#+begin_src lisp
  (css-property-unitless-p property)
#+end_src

Return =T= if a CSS property should be unitless.
********* =css-emit-value=
#+begin_src lisp
  (css-emit-value value &optional property)
#+end_src

Emit a CSS value, adding =px= where appropriate.
********* =css-split-body=
#+begin_src lisp
  (css-split-body body)
#+end_src

Split CSS DSL bodies into declarations and nested rules.
********* =register-css-emitters=
#+begin_src lisp
  (register-css-emitters target)
#+end_src

********* =css-expand-rule=

#+end_src

Expand nested CSS DSL rules into normalized internal forms.
******** Key Forms
********* =css-decl=
#+begin_src lisp
  (css-decl property value)
#+end_src

Emit a CSS declaration.
********* =css-rule=

#+end_src

Emit a CSS rule block.
********* =css-nested-rule=
#+begin_src lisp
  (css-nested-rule parent selector declarations &rest nested)
#+end_src

Emit a nested CSS rule.
********* =css-at-rule=
#+begin_src lisp

#+end_src

Emit an at-rule wrapping a selector.
********* =css-at-rule-bare=
#+begin_src lisp
  (css-at-rule-bare at-rule declarations)
#+end_src

Emit a declaration-only at-rule.
********* =css-stylesheet=
#+begin_src lisp
  (css-stylesheet &rest rules)
#+end_src

Emit a full stylesheet.

******* redwood target
The =redwood-target.lisp= component builds on the TypeScript target to generate RedwoodSDK-style Cloudflare/React applications.

Key capabilities include:
- JSX emitters and HTML tag macros
- =defcomponent=, =defclient=, =defaction=
- =defconfig= for =package.json=
- =deftsconfig=
- =defviteconfig=
- =defwrangler=
- =defapp=
- auto-emission of default config files during finalize
******** State Variables
- =*redwood-has-css-import*= :: Tracks detected CSS imports during compilation.
- =*redwood-env-bindings*= :: Tracks inferred environment bindings.
- =*redwood-wrangler-sections*= :: Tracks explicitly configured wrangler sections.
- =*redwood-default-import-sources*= :: Sources that should use default imports.

********* =check-result=
Structure representing the result of a check. It has slots:

- =message=: The warning/error message string.
- =form=: The Lisp form that failed the check.

#+end_src
