****** core and other
Hactar is built around an extensible architecture using hooks and macros. If you are a LISPer you will feel right at home.

- *Hooks*: A publish/subscribe system (=nhooks=) that allows different parts of the application to react to events, such as file changes
  (=*file-event-hook*=) or LLM responses (=*process-history-hook*=).
- *Analyzers*: Functions that attach to hooks to analyze events and gather information about the project.
  For example, an analyzer might inspect a =package.json= file to determine the project's dependencies. Defined with =def-analyzer=.
- *Rules*: Functions that attach to hooks and dynamically modify the LLM's system prompt based on the current context.
  For example, a rule could add React-specific instructions to the prompt if it detects a
  React project. Defined with =defrule=.
- *Processors*: Functions that run after an LLM response is received.
  They are attached to the =*process-history-hook*= and are responsible for parsing and acting on the LLM's output, such as applying =SEARCH/REPLACE= blocks. Defined with =def-processor=.
- *Watchers*: Background processes that monitor external commands (like
  a test suite). Their output can be hooked into by analyzers. Defined with =defwatcher=.
- *Tools*: Functions that the LLM can decide to call to perform actions or get information.
  Hactar exposes these tools to the LLM, which can then request to execute them with specific arguments. Defined with =deftool=.
- *Commands*: User-facing commands callable from the REPL. Slash commands (e.g., =/help=) are for direct user interaction, while dot commands (e.g., =.cat=) are designed to be interpreted by the LLM as part of a prompt. Defined with =define-command= and =defdot=.
******* Data Structures
******** model-config
A struct holding the configuration for a specific LLM.

- =name= (String):
  The unique name for the model configuration (e.g., ="openai/gpt-4o-mini"=).
- =provider= (String):
  The provider name (e.g., ="openai"=), derived from the name.
- =model-name= (String):
  The actual model identifier used by the provider's API.
- =edit-format= (String):
  The format for code edits (="diff"= or ="file"=).
- =use-repo-map= (Boolean):
  Whether to include the repository map in the context for this model.
- =max-output-tokens= (Integer):
  The maximum number of tokens the model can generate.
- =max-input-tokens= (Integer):
  The maximum number of tokens the model can accept as input.
- =input-cost-per-token= (Float):
  The cost per input token.
- =output-cost-per-token= (Float):
  The cost per output token.
- =supports= (List of Strings):
  A list of features the model supports (e.g., ="vision"=).
******** web-route struct
#+begin_src lisp
  (defstruct web-route
               "Represents a route within a web command."
    name           ; Route name (symbol)
    description    ; Route description (string)
    pattern        ; List pattern to match, e.g., ("newest" &rest args)
    priority       ; Integer priority (higher = checked first)
    handler        ; Function that returns code to execute
    bindings)      ; List of variable names to bind from the pattern
#+end_src

A web-route is a pattern used to match a web command to web route. It is the core struct for the web commands in Hactar. The stuff like =hactar hn latest= gets routed using it.
********* Example
Use the macro to construct a web-route:

#+begin_src lisp
  (defwebroute hn-top
               "Get the top items from hn"
   ("top" &rest args) (args)
   :priority 10
   (lambda () (get-hn-top args)))
#+end_src
******** web-command struct
#+begin_src lisp
  (defstruct web-command
    "Represents a web command with routes."
    name           ; Command name (string)
    description    ; Command description
    routes         ; List of web-route structs
    default-route) ; Default route handler (optional)
#+end_src
******* Macros
These macros are the primary way to extend Hactar's functionality.
******** def-analyzer
#+begin_src lisp
  (def-analyzer name hooks enabled (&rest args) &body body)
#+end_src

Defines an analyzer function and registers it with the system.

- =name=: A symbol for the analyzer's name.
- =hooks=: A list of hook specifications to attach to. A spec can be a hook variable (e.g., =*file-event-hook*=) or a list
  =(hook-variable filter-function)=.
- =enabled=: A boolean indicating if the analyzer is enabled by default.
- =args=: The argument list for the analyzer function, which must match the signature of the hooks it attaches to.
- =body=: The code for the analyzer.
******** defrule
#+begin_src lisp
  (defrule name hook-spec (&rest args) &body body)
#+end_src

Defines a rule that can dynamically add text to the system prompt.

- =name=: A symbol for the rule's name.
- =hook-spec=: The hook specification to attach to (same format as
  =def-analyzer=).
- =args=: The argument list for the rule function.
- =body=: The code for the rule. It should return a string to be added to the prompt, or =NIL= to remove/deactivate the rule.
******** defwatcher
#+begin_src lisp
  (defwatcher name command help &key (daemon nil))
#+end_src

Defines a watcher process that can be started by the user.

- =name=: A symbol for the watcher's name.
- =command=: A string or list of strings for the shell command to run.
- =help=: A help string describing the watcher.
- =daemon=: A boolean. If =T=, the watcher runs continuously in the background. If =NIL=, it runs once and exits.
******** def-processor
#+begin_src lisp
  (def-processor name (&rest args) &body body)
#+end_src

Defines a processor that runs on every LLM response. It is automatically attached to the =*process-history-hook*=.

- =name=: A symbol for the processor's name.
- =args=: The argument list. For the history hook, this is typically
  =(history)=.
- =body=: The code for the processor.
******** deftool
#+begin_src lisp
  (deftool name schema &body body &key (permissions :confirm))
#+end_src

Defines a tool that the LLM can call.

- =name=: A symbol for the tool's name.
- =schema=:
  A plist describing the tool's name, description, and parameters in a format compatible with the LLM provider (e.g., OpenAI's function calling schema).
- =body=:
  The Lisp code to execute when the tool is called. The arguments from the LLM are available in a plist bound to =args=.
- =permissions=:
  =:confirm= (default) requires user confirmation before running, while =:auto= allows the tool to run automatically.
******** define-command
#+begin_src lisp
  (define-command name args &body body)
#+end_src

Define a command, available as a slash command and/or a sub-command.
   Use :slash and :sub keyword arguments at the end of the body to control availability.
   :slash defaults to t, :sub defaults to nil.
   Use :cli-options to define CLI arguments for the sub-command.
   When used as a sub-command, the body receives a plist of parsed arguments
- =name=:
  A symbol or string for the command name. The leading =/= is added automatically.
- =args=:
  The argument list for the command function.
- =body=:
  The code for the command. The first string in the body is used as the docstring.

Options:
- =:slash=: Make it a slash command. Defaults to =t=
- =:sub=: Make it a sub command. Defaults to =nil= (i.e false)
- =:cli-options= A plist of CLI arguments
********* Examples
#+begin_src lisp
  (define-command docs-db (args)
    "List all known documentation and select one. In non-interactive mode, prints the path of the selected doc.
  Options: -t/--tags <tag>, -l/--limit <n>"
    (run-docs-db args)
    :cli-options ((:short "t" :long "tags" :description "Filter by tags")
                  (:short "l" :long "limit" :description "Limit number of results")))
#+end_src
******** define-sub-command
#+begin_src lisp
  define-sub-command (name args &body body)
#+end_src

Define a sub-command for CLI use. Sets *in-repl* to nil.
   NAME can be a symbol or a string (e.g., 'my-cmd', \"my.cmd\").
   Supports :cli-options keyword for defining command-line arguments.
   The command body receives a plist of parsed arguments.

- =name=:
  A symbol or string for the command name. The leading =/= is added automatically.
- =args=:
  The argument list for the command function.
- =body=:
  The code for the command. The first string in the body is used as the docstring.

Options:
- =:cli-options= A plist of CLI arguments
******** define-slash-command
#+begin_src lisp
  define-slash-command (name args &body body)
#+end_src

Define a slash command with the given name and arguments, capturing the docstring.
   NAME can be a symbol or a string (e.g., 'my-cmd', \"my.cmd\", \"/my.other.cmd\").
   Supports :cli-options keyword for defining command-line arguments.
   The command body receives a plist of parsed arguments if cli-options are present
- =name=:
  A symbol or string for the command name. The leading =/= is added automatically.
- =args=:
  The argument list for the command function.
- =body=:
  The code for the command. The first string in the body is used as the docstring.

Options:
- =:cli-options= A plist of CLI arguments
******** defdot
#+begin_src lisp
  (defdot name args &body body)
#+end_src

Defines a dot command (e.g., =.cat=) intended for the LLM to use.

- =name=:
  A symbol for the command name. The leading =.= is added automatically.
- =args=:
  The argument list for the command function.
- =body=:
  The code for the command. The first string in the body is used as the docstring.
******** defagent
Define an agent that can be run to perform tasks.

The body should contain a docstring (optional) followed by keyword arguments:
   :stack (optional list of strings)
   :init (required form)
   :run (optional form)
   :stop-condition (optional form)
   :cleanup (optional form
******** defwebcommand
#+begin_src lisp
  (defmacro defwebcommand (name description &rest route-definitions)
    "Define a web command with routes. ")
#+end_src

Used for constructing web commands to allow Hactar and you to retrieve things as plaintext. The underlying mechanism behind how Hactar can retrieve API docs for npm packages, get plain rss feeds for sites etc.
********* Example
#+begin_src lisp
  (defwebcommand hn
    "Fetch news from Hacker News"
    (defwebroute ("newest" &rest args) (args)
      :priority 10
      `(get-hn-newest ',args))
    (def-default-route ()
      `(get-hn-front-page-md)))
#+end_src
******** defwebroute
#+begin_src lisp
  (defmacro defwebroute (name description pattern bindings &rest args)
    "Define a route within a defwebcommand. Pattern is matched against args.
     NAME is a symbol identifying this route.
     DESCRIPTION is a string documenting what this route does.
     PATTERN is matched against args.
     BINDINGS specifies which variables from the pattern to bind.
     Body should return code to execute.
     Accepts :priority keyword (default 10) followed by body forms."
#+end_src
A web-route is a pattern used to match a web command to web route. It is the core struct for the web commands in Hactar. The stuff like =hactar hn latest= gets routed using it.
********* Example
#+begin_src lisp
  (defwebroute newest-hn
               "Newest items on HN"
               ("top" &rest args) (args)
               :priority 10
               (lambda () (get-hn-top args)))
#+end_src

*Note*: You must use the defwebroute macro inside of defwebcommand. This is so the scoping ends up correct
******** def-default-route
#+begin_src lisp
  (defmacro def-default-route (bindings &body body)
    "Define a default route for a web command (when no other routes match).")
#+end_src
******** defdoc
A macro for defining documentation in the current context/hactar instance. The macro is the primary macro used to integrate knowledge bases with Hactar. We use a combination of hooks, regex, ML models etc to add docs to context but it ultimately just boils down a push of a plist onto the *docs* global.
********* Examples
#+begin_src lisp
  (defdoc "Example Doc" "file:docs/example.txt" :tags '("example" "test") :covers '("example-cover"))
#+end_src
******** deferror
#+begin_src lisp
  (deferror title &rest args)
#+end_src

Define an error document in the current context/hactar instance. This macro pushes an error plist onto the =*errors*= global.

Required keys:
- =:code=
- =:stack=
- =:message=
- =:cause=
- =:solution=

Optional keys:
- =:slug=
- =:tags=
********* Examples
#+begin_src lisp
  (deferror "Example Error"
            :code "E123"
            :stack "Error Stack"
            :message "An error occurred"
            :cause "Something went wrong"
            :solution "Fix it")
#+end_src
******* Core Functions
******** start-agent
#+begin_src lisp
  (start-agent agent-def args)
#+end_src

Creates an agent instance and starts its execution loop in a new thread.

- =agent-def=: The agent definition struct.
- =args=: Arguments to pass to the agent's init function.

*Return Value:* The started agent instance.
******** stop-agent
#+begin_src lisp
  (stop-agent agent-id)
#+end_src

Stops a running agent by its ID.

- =agent-id=: The ID of the agent to stop.
******** get-llm-response
#+begin_src lisp
  (get-llm-response prompt &key stream custom-system-prompt add-to-history dot-command-p)
#+end_src

The main function for interacting with the current LLM.

- =prompt= (String): The user's prompt.
- =&key=:
  - =stream= (Boolean):
    Whether to stream the response.
  - =custom-system-prompt= (String):
    An override for the system prompt.
  - =add-to-history= (Boolean):
    Whether to add this turn to the chat history.
  - =dot-command-p= (Boolean):
    If =T=, uses the specialized dot-command system prompt.
******** add-to-chat-history
#+begin_src lisp
  (add-to-chat-history role content &key tool-calls tool_call_id name)
#+end_src

Adds a message to the global =*chat-history*=.

- =role= (String): ="user"=, ="assistant"=, or ="tool"=.
- =content= (String): The text content of the message.
- =&key=: Optional parameters for tool-related messages.
******* Available Hooks
Extensions can attach to these hooks to react to events.

- =*file-event-hook*=: Fired on file system changes. Handler receives
  =(pathname event-type)=.
- =*raw-file-event-hook*=: Raw filesystem watcher hook, includes files in the git-ignored =.hactar= instance directory. Handler receives =(pathname event-type)=.
- =*package-json-analyzed-hook*=: Fired after a =package.json= file is analyzed. Handler receives =(metadata-hashtable)=.
- =*process-history-hook*=: Fired after any LLM response is added to the history. Handler receives =(full-chat-history)=.
- =*assistant-extraction-hook*=:
  Fired when the assistant mode extracts new text from the screen. Handler receives =(extraction-text)=.
- =*watcher-<name>-output-hook*=:
  A dynamic hook is created for each watcher defined with =defwatcher=. For a watcher named =test=, the hook is =*watcher-test-output-hook*=.
  Handler receives =(active-watcher-struct line-of-output)=.
- =*watcher-test-watcher-output-hook*=: Fired when test watcher output is received. Handler receives =(active-watcher line-of-output)=.
- =*context-file-added-hook*=:
  Called when a new file is addeded to context. The handler is called with the file path (string).
- =*context-file-dropped-hook*=:
  Called when a file is dropped from context. The handler is called with the file path (string).
- =*context-variable-changed-hook*=: Fired when a context variable changes. Handler receives =(variable-keyword new-value)=.
- =*context-doc-added-hook*=: Called when a documentation page is added to context. Handler receives =(doc-alist)=.
- =*context-doc-dropped-hook*=: Called when a documentation page is dropped from context. Handler receives =(doc-id)=.
- =*model-changed-hook*=: Hook run when =*current-model*= changes. Handler receives =(new-model old-model)=.
- =*stack-changed-hook*=:
  Fired when the stack variable changes. Handler receives the new stack list.
- =*history-changed-hook*=: Fired when chat history is modified. Handler receives no arguments.
- =*org-heading-parsed-hook*=: Fired when an Org-mode heading is parsed. Handler receives =(heading-plist)=.
- =*concept-created-hook*=: Fired when a new concept is created in the monolith. Handler receives =(org-concept-struct)=.
- =*concept-matured-hook*=: Fired when a concept maturity level changes. Handler receives =(org-concept old-maturity new-maturity)=.
- =*tangle-completed-hook*=: Fired when tangling finishes. Handler receives =(tangle-result-struct)=.
- =*drift-detected-hook*=: Fired when drift is detected between source files and tangled files. Handler receives =(drift-list)=.
- =*link-resolved-hook*=: Fired when an org link is resolved. Handler receives =(link-uri target)=.
- =*litmode-scope-changed-hook*=: Fired when the active litmode scope changes. Handler receives =(new-scope old-scope)=.
- =*litmode-tangle-completed-hook*=: Fired when litmode tangling completes. Handler receives =(tangle-results-list)=.
- =*litmode-task-transitioned-hook*=: Fired when a litmode task transitions states. Handler receives =(task-id new-state old-state)=.
- =*litmode-drift-detected-hook*=: Fired when litmode drift is detected. Handler receives =(drift-list)=.
- =*proxy-request-hook*=: Fired when LLM proxy intercepts an upstream request. Handler receives =(request-alist)= and can return a modified request.
- =*proxy-response-hook*=: Fired when LLM proxy intercepts an upstream response. Handler receives =(response-alist request-alist)= and can return a modified response.
******* Hook Usage Examples
****** Code as Value API
Hactar models code fragments as immutable semantic "values" using =code-value= structs. Transformations to a code-value (such as editing or describing) generate new code-values, preserving the parent and providing a full history/provenance chain.
******* Data Structures
******** code-value
An immutable semantic wrapper around code.

- Slots/Fields:
  - =id=: A unique string ID.
  - =name=: Optional name or symbol for this selection.
  - =source-file=: Pathname of the source file.
  - =source-region=: Cons cell representing line range =(start . end)=.
  - =source-text=: String of the actual code.
  - =language=: String language identifier (e.g. ="typescript"=).
  - =intent=: String describing the purpose of the code.
  - =inputs=: List of input descriptions.
  - =outputs=: List of output descriptions.
  - =effects=: List of side effects.
  - =invariants=: List of invariants.
  - =parent=: Parent =code-value= in the transformation chain.
  - =staged-p=: T if staged for application.
  - =applied-p=: T if applied to disk.
******* Core Functions
******** hactar-init
#+begin_src lisp
  (hactar-init)
#+end_src

Initializes Hactar context, ensuring repository root, models, and databases are loaded.
******** code/select
#+begin_src lisp
  (code/select source &key function class method region name)
#+end_src

Select code from a source (file path or specifier) and wrap it as a code-value.
******** code/from-string
#+begin_src lisp
  (code/from-string text &key language name)
#+end_src

Create a code-value from a string of code.
******** code/from-context
#+begin_src lisp
  (code/from-context file-path)
#+end_src

Create a code-value from a file already in the Hactar context.
******** code/describe
#+begin_src lisp
  (code/describe cv &key force)
#+end_src

Populate semantic fields of a code-value using the LLM.
******** code/source
#+begin_src lisp
  (code/source cv)
#+end_src

Return the source text of a code-value.
******** code/intent
#+begin_src lisp
  (code/intent cv)
#+end_src

Return the intent of a code-value, computing it via LLM if necessary.
******** code/ask
#+begin_src lisp
  (code/ask cv question)
#+end_src

Ask a question about the code-value and return the response.
******** code/history
#+begin_src lisp
  (code/history cv)
#+end_src

Return the chain of transformations that led to this code-value.
******** code/parent
#+begin_src lisp
  (code/parent cv)
#+end_src

Return the parent code-value.
******** code/original
#+begin_src lisp
  (code/original cv)
#+end_src

Return the root/original code-value in the transformation chain.
******** code/show
#+begin_src lisp
  (code/show cv &key (stream *standard-output*))
#+end_src

Display a code-value with all its metadata to the given stream.
******** code/summary
#+begin_src lisp
  (code/summary cv)
#+end_src

Return a short summary string for a code-value.
****** Hydra API
The Hydra API allows defining interactive, transient menus inside Hactar's terminal interface (both TUI and standard CLI).
******* Special Variables
- =*hydras*=: Global hash table storing all registered hydras.
- =*hydra-input*=: Override stream for hydra input (useful for scripting/testing).
- =*hydra-output*=: Override stream for hydra output.
******* Macros and Functions
******** defhydra
#+begin_src lisp
  (defhydra name options &body body)
#+end_src

Define a transient/hydra menu command and subcommands.
******** run-hydra
#+begin_src lisp
  (run-hydra hydra)
#+end_src

Run the interactive loop for a given hydra.
****** lsp
The =lsp.lisp= component exposes Hactar as a Language Server Protocol server over stdio.

It currently focuses on diagnostics and a provider architecture so different analyzers or checkers can contribute editor-visible issues.
******* lsp-diagnostic
Structure describing a single diagnostic, including:
- start and end line/column
- severity
- source
- message
******* deflsp-provider
#+begin_src lisp
  (deflsp-provider name &body body)
#+end_src

Define a diagnostic provider.

Important keys:
- =:languages=: Language IDs handled by the provider.
- =:enabled=: Whether it is active by default.

The implementation receives =(source file-path)= and returns a list of =lsp-diagnostic= structs.
******* lsp-collect-diagnostics
#+begin_src lisp
  (lsp-collect-diagnostics source file-path language-id)
#+end_src

Run all matching providers and collect diagnostics for a document.
******* lsp-publish-diagnostics
#+begin_src lisp
  (lsp-publish-diagnostics uri)
#+end_src

Publish diagnostics for an open document using =textDocument/publishDiagnostics=.
******* start-lsp
#+begin_src lisp
  (start-lsp)
#+end_src

Start the LSP server.
******* hactar lsp
#+begin_src
  hactar lsp
#+end_src

Run Hactar as an LSP server over stdio.
****** router
This file provides a generic router using regex pattern matching. It is used by =import.lisp= and other subsystems that need declarative string-to-handler dispatch.
******* defroute
#+begin_src lisp
  (defroute pattern args &rest rest-args)
#+end_src

Define a route with regex pattern matching.

- =pattern=: A regex pattern string with capture groups.
- =args=: Lambda list for the handler function (receives extracted params).
- =:params=: List of parameter names corresponding to regex capture groups.
- =:priority=: Integer priority for route matching (default 10, higher = checked first).
- =body=: Code to execute when route matches.
******* register-route
#+begin_src lisp
  (register-route name pattern param-names priority handler)
#+end_src

Register a route in the global routes table.

- =name=: Route name (symbol).
- =pattern=: Regex pattern string.
- =param-names=: List of parameter names to extract from regex groups.
- =priority=: Integer priority.
- =handler=: Function that handles the route.
******* match-route
#+begin_src lisp
  (match-route input)
#+end_src

Try to match input against all registered routes.

- =input=: The string to match against route patterns.

*Return Value:* (values route params) or (values nil nil).
******* execute-route
#+begin_src lisp
  (execute-route input)
#+end_src

Match and execute a route for the given input string.

- =input=: The string to match.

*Return Value:* The result of the route handler, or NIL if no match.
******* defflag
#+begin_src lisp
  (defflag name aliases lambda-list &body body)
#+end_src

Define a CLI flag.

- =name=: Keyword identifier (e.g. =:model=).
- =aliases=: List of alias strings (e.g. ='("--model" "-m")=).
- =lambda-list=: =()= for boolean flags, or =(value)= for value flags.
- =body=: Code to execute when the flag is parsed, optionally starting with keywords:
  - =:description=: Documentation string for the flag.
  - =:takes-value=: Boolean indicating if it takes a value (derived from lambda-list if omitted).
  - =:examples=: List of example usage strings.
  - =:validator=: Lambda function called to validate the value.
  - =:initializer=: Lambda function called once during system setup.
  - =:error-level=: Symbol indicating severity of validation failure (=:warning= or =:error=).
****** gen
Generative commands that use LLMs to generate code or configuration.

The =gen.lisp= layer is Hactar's higher-level scaffolding system. It sits above raw SEARCH/REPLACE editing and lets you define generators, patterns, and recipes that can mix deterministic operations with LLM planning.
******* Variables
- =*generators*= :: Registry of all generators.
- =*active-generators*= :: Registry of active generators.
- =*patterns*= :: Registry of all patterns.
- =*active-patterns*= :: Registry of active patterns.
- =*registries*= :: Registry metadata for tracked artifacts.
- =*recipes*= :: Registry of recipes.
- =*gen-history*= :: History of generation runs.
- =*gen-history-limit*= :: Maximum retained generation history entries.
******* Data Structures
******** =gen-operation=
Represents an atomic generation action.
******** =gen-result=
Represents the outcome of executing a generation plan.
******** =generator=
Represents a generator definition.
******** =pattern=
Represents a reusable pattern definition.
******** =registry=
Represents a tracked registry type.
******** =recipe=
Represents a multi-step recipe.
******** =framework-analyzer=
Represents a framework-specific analyzer with reusable queries.
