****** npm
NPM package management and documentation utilities.

This layer wraps the npm registry and package metadata so Hactar can fetch docs, package metadata, and search results without relying entirely on an LLM.
******* get-npm-docs
#+begin_src lisp
  (get-npm-docs package-name &optional version-spec)
#+end_src

Get documentation for an NPM package. First checks custom doc routes, then falls back to package README.

- =package-name=: The name of the npm package.
- =version-spec=: Optional version string (defaults to "latest").

*Return Value:* A string containing the documentation.
******* search-npm-packages
#+begin_src lisp
  (search-npm-packages query &key (limit 20))
#+end_src

Search NPM packages and return results.

- =query=: The search query string.
- =limit=: Maximum number of results.

*Return Value:* A list of package objects.
****** proxy
The =proxy.lisp= component implements an OpenRouter-compatible chat-completions proxy that injects Hactar context into upstream requests.
******* Proxy Hooks
- =*proxy-request-hook*= :: Composed request mutation hook.
- =*proxy-response-hook*= :: Response inspection/mutation hook.
******* Core Functions
******** =proxy-extract-system-prompt=
#+begin_src lisp
  (proxy-extract-system-prompt messages)
#+end_src

Extract and merge system messages from a messages array.

*Return Value:* Two values:
1. System prompt string or =NIL=
2. Non-system message list
******** =proxy-build-context-section=
#+begin_src lisp
  (proxy-build-context-section)
#+end_src

Build the injected proxy context section.
******** =proxy-inject-context=
#+begin_src lisp
  (proxy-inject-context request-plist)
#+end_src

Inject Hactar context into a request plist.
******** =proxy-reassemble-messages=
#+begin_src lisp
  (proxy-reassemble-messages system-prompt messages)
#+end_src

Rebuild a messages vector with a synthetic system message if needed.
******** =proxy-forward-request=
#+begin_src lisp
  (proxy-forward-request request-plist)
#+end_src

Forward a processed request upstream.

*Return Value:* Raw upstream values and a type marker.
******** =proxy-extract-request-headers=
#+begin_src lisp
  (proxy-extract-request-headers env)
#+end_src

Extract relevant headers from Lack env.
******** =handle-proxy-request=
#+begin_src lisp
  (handle-proxy-request params env)
#+end_src

Main proxy route handler.
******** =register-proxy-routes=
#+begin_src lisp
  (register-proxy-routes)
#+end_src

Register proxy routes on the Ningle app.
******** =start-proxy=
#+begin_src lisp
  (start-proxy &key (port *proxy-port*))
#+end_src

Start the proxy and ensure the HTTP server is running.
******** =proxy-messages-contain-p=
#+begin_src lisp
  (proxy-messages-contain-p messages &rest search-strings)
#+end_src

Return =T= if any message contains one of the provided substrings.
******** =proxy-model-matches-p=
#+begin_src lisp
  (proxy-model-matches-p model &rest patterns)
#+end_src

Return =T= if a model string matches a provided substring pattern.
******* Commands
******** =/proxy.start=
#+begin_src
  /proxy.start
#+end_src

Start the proxy.
******** =/proxy.status=
#+begin_src
  /proxy.status
#+end_src

Show proxy status and configuration.
****** processors
Functions for parsing and applying LLM output blocks.

Processors are one of the most important extension points in Hactar. They run after assistant output is added to history, which makes them ideal for turning plain model output into concrete effects like file edits, file creation, tool execution, or follow-up prompts.
******* parse-file-blocks
#+begin_src lisp
  (parse-file-blocks text)
#+end_src

Parses file creation blocks from text. Expects markdown code blocks with a filename in the opening fence.

- =text=: The string containing markdown code blocks.

*Return Value:* A list of alists, where each alist represents a file block: =((:filename . "path") (:content . "content"))=.
******* apply-file-blocks
#+begin_src lisp
  (apply-file-blocks file-blocks)
#+end_src

Processes a list of file blocks, creating them if they don't exist and user confirms.

- =file-blocks=: A list of alists as returned by =parse-file-blocks=.
******* parse-search-replace-blocks
#+begin_src lisp
  (parse-search-replace-blocks text)
#+end_src

Parses SEARCH/REPLACE blocks from the given text using a line-by-line state machine.

- =text=: The string containing SEARCH/REPLACE blocks.

*Return Value:* A list of plists, each representing a block: ='((:filename "path/to/file") (:search "search text") (:replace "replace text"))=.
******* apply-search-replace-blocks
#+begin_src lisp
  (apply-search-replace-blocks blocks &key (autocommit *git-autocommit*))
#+end_src

Applies the changes defined in the parsed blocks list to the filesystem.

- =blocks=: A list of plists as returned by =parse-search-replace-blocks=.
- =autocommit=: Boolean, if T, performs a git commit after applying changes.
****** create
The =create.lisp= component powers starter-based project creation. It combines a starter guide, repository context, and a create-specific system prompt to generate a new codebase.
******* create-project
#+begin_src lisp
  (create-project starter user-prompt)
#+end_src

Create a new project from a starter guide.

- =starter=: Either a known starter name such as ="react"= or ="sinatra"=, a file path, or a pathname to a starter file.
- =user-prompt=: Natural-language description of the project to generate.

*Behavior:*
- Loads starter content from the built-in starters path or the provided file.
- Renders the =system.create.org= prompt using the current language and generated context.
- Sends the final prompt to the selected model.
- Adds the interaction to chat history.
******* /create
#+begin_src
  /create <starter> <prompt...>
#+end_src

Create a new project from a starter inside the current repository context.
******* hactar create
#+begin_src
  hactar create --path <dir> [--starter <starter>] <prompt...>
#+end_src

Create a new project in a target directory. This subcommand:
- Ensures the target directory exists.
- Initializes a git repository if one is missing.
- Sets =*repo-root*= to the target directory.
- Invokes =create-project= with the requested starter.
******* /create.agent
#+begin_src
  /create.agent [prompt...]
#+end_src

Create a new agent-oriented project using the Agent starter guide.
****** processors
******* deftool (Macro)
#+begin_src lisp
  (deftool name (&rest params) &body body)
#+end_src

Define a tool that Hactar's LLM can invoke. The tool is registered in =*defined-tools*= under a snake_case version of =NAME=.

- =name= (Symbol): The tool name. Converted to snake_case (e.g. =read-file= becomes =read_file=).
- =params=: A list of parameter specifications. Each is either:
  - A bare symbol (defaults to a required string parameter), or
  - =(param-name type &key description required enum)= where =type= is one of =:string=, =:boolean=, =:number=, =:array=.
- Body keyword options (must appear before implementation code):
  - =:description= (String, required): Human-readable description of what the tool does.
  - =:rules= (String, optional): Usage rules/guidelines included in the tool's XML description.
  - =:permissions= (Keyword, optional): =:confirm= (default) requires user/rule approval; =:auto= allows automatic execution.
- Body: Implementation code. The plist of parsed arguments is available as =hactar::args=.

Example:
#+begin_src lisp
  (deftool read-file ((path :string :description "File path" :required t))
    :description "Read contents of a file"
    :rules "Only read files within the project directory"
    :permissions :confirm
    (let ((file-path (getf args :path)))
      (uiop:read-file-string file-path)))
#+end_src
******* tool-definition (Struct)
#+begin_src lisp
  (make-tool-definition :name :description :parameters :rules :permissions :function)
#+end_src

Structure representing a defined tool.

- =name= (String): The snake_case tool name.
- =description= (String): Human-readable description.
- =parameters= (List): List of =tool-parameter= structs.
- =rules= (String or NIL): Optional usage rules/guidelines.
- =permissions= (Keyword): =:confirm= or =:auto=.
- =function= (Function): The implementing function.
******* tool-parameter (Struct)
#+begin_src lisp
  (make-tool-parameter :name :type :description :required :enum)
#+end_src

Structure representing a tool parameter.

- =name= (String): Parameter name.
- =type= (Keyword): One of =:string=, =:boolean=, =:number=, =:array=.
- =description= (String): Human-readable description.
- =required= (Boolean): Whether the parameter is required (default =T=).
- =enum= (List or NIL): Optional list of allowed string values.
******* generate-tool-xml-description
#+begin_src lisp
  (generate-tool-xml-description tool)
#+end_src

Generate an XML description string for a single =tool-definition=. Used when tools are embedded in the system prompt (=*tools-in-system-prompt*= is =T=).

- =tool= (tool-definition): The tool to describe.

Returns a string containing the XML representation including =<tool>=, =<description>=, =<parameters>=, =<rules>=, and =<usage>= elements.
******* generate-all-tools-xml
#+begin_src lisp
  (generate-all-tools-xml)
#+end_src

Generate XML descriptions for all defined tools, wrapped in a =<tools>= element. Only produces output when =*tool-use-enabled*= and =*tools-in-system-prompt*= are both =T= and at least one tool is defined.

Returns a string or =NIL=.
******* tool-definition-to-api-format
#+begin_src lisp
  (tool-definition-to-api-format tool)
#+end_src

Convert a =tool-definition= to the OpenAI/Anthropic API tool-calling format (an alist with =:type "function"= and a =:function= sub-alist containing =:name=, =:description=, and =:parameters= in JSON Schema form).

- =tool= (tool-definition): The tool to convert.
******* get-tools-for-api
#+begin_src lisp
  (get-tools-for-api)
#+end_src

Get all defined tools formatted as a vector of API-format alists. Only returns results when =*tool-use-enabled*= is =T= and =*tools-in-system-prompt*= is =NIL=.

Returns a vector or =NIL=.
******* parse-xml-tool-calls
#+begin_src lisp
  (parse-xml-tool-calls text)
#+end_src

Parse XML tool invocations from an LLM response string. Looks for =<tool_name>...</tool_name>= blocks matching registered tools.

- =text= (String): The LLM response text to parse.

Returns a list of =(tool-name . args-alist)= pairs.
******* parse-xml-tool-args
#+begin_src lisp
  (parse-xml-tool-args content tool-name)
#+end_src

Parse individual XML parameter elements from within a tool call block.

- =content= (String): The inner XML content of the tool call.
- =tool-name= (String): The name of the tool (used to look up parameter definitions).

Returns an alist of =(keyword . value)= pairs, with values coerced according to parameter types.
******* execute-tool
#+begin_src lisp
  (execute-tool tool-name args)
#+end_src

Execute a registered tool by name. Checks permissions via =resolve-permission= before running.

- =tool-name= (String): The snake_case name of the tool.
- =args= (Alist or Plist): The parameter values.

Returns =(values result success-p error-message)=.
******* execute-xml-tool-calls
#+begin_src lisp
  (execute-xml-tool-calls tool-calls)
#+end_src

Execute a list of parsed XML tool calls (as returned by =parse-xml-tool-calls=).

- =tool-calls= (List): List of =(tool-name . args-alist)= pairs.

Returns a list of =(tool-name result success-p error-msg)= for each call.
******* handle-api-tool-calls
#+begin_src lisp
  (handle-api-tool-calls tool-calls-list)
#+end_src

Handle tool calls received in the LLM API's native format. Executes each tool and returns message alists suitable for appending to the conversation (with =:role "tool"=).

- =tool-calls-list= (List): List of tool call alists in API format (with =:id=, =:function= containing =:name= and =:arguments=).

Returns a list of tool result message alists.
******* format-tool-results-for-prompt
#+begin_src lisp
  (format-tool-results-for-prompt results)
#+end_src

Format tool execution results as an XML =<tool_results>= block for inclusion in a follow-up prompt.

- =results= (List): List of =(tool-name output success-p error-msg)= as returned by =execute-xml-tool-calls=.

Returns a string.
******* /tool-call (Command)
#+begin_src
  /tool-call <tool_name> [key=value ...]
#+end_src

Manually invoke a defined tool from the REPL. Parameters are given as =key=value= pairs.
******* /tools (Command)
#+begin_src
  /tools
#+end_src

List all available tools and their descriptions, parameters, and current mode (XML-in-system-prompt or API).
******* /tools-mode (Command)
#+begin_src
  /tools-mode [prompt|api]
#+end_src

Toggle or set the tools mode. With no arguments, toggles between XML-in-system-prompt and API mode. Pass =prompt= or =api= to set explicitly.
******* Built-in Tools
******** execute_command
#+begin_src lisp
  (deftool execute-command ((command :string ...) (requires_approval :boolean ...))
    :permissions :confirm ...)
#+end_src

Execute a CLI command on the system. Set =requires_approval= to =true= for potentially impactful operations. Commands run in the current working directory.
******** read_file
#+begin_src lisp
  (deftool read-file ((path :string ...))
    :permissions :auto ...)
#+end_src

Read the contents of a file and add it to the context. The file path is relative to the repository root.
******** write_to_file
#+begin_src lisp
  (deftool write-to-file ((path :string ...) (content :string ...))
    :permissions :confirm ...)
#+end_src

Write complete content to a file. Creates the file and any needed directories if they don't exist. Overwrites existing files.
******** replace_in_file
#+begin_src lisp
  (deftool replace-in-file ((path :string ...) (search :string ...) (replace :string ...))
    :permissions :confirm ...)
#+end_src

Replace the first occurrence of exact =search= text with =replace= text in a file. The search must match character-for-character including whitespace.
****** Permissions System
******* permission-rule (Struct)
#+begin_src lisp
  (make-permission-rule :name :priority :tool-pattern :predicate :description :source)
#+end_src

A rule that determines whether a tool call is allowed, denied, or needs confirmation.

- =name= (String): Unique name for the rule.
- =priority= (Integer): Higher values are checked first.
- =tool-pattern=: A string (exact tool name match) or =:any= (matches all tools).
- =predicate= (Function): =(lambda (tool-name args))= returning =:allow=, =:deny=, =:confirm=, or =:abstain=.
- =description= (String): Human-readable description.
- =source= (Keyword): Origin — =:system=, =:user=, =:mode=, or =:session=.
******* session-override (Struct)
#+begin_src lisp
  (make-session-override :tool-name :match-type :args-fingerprint :decision)
#+end_src

A runtime override created from interactive confirmations. Session overrides take precedence over all rules.

- =tool-name= (String): The tool this override applies to.
- =match-type= (Keyword): =:exact-args= (matches specific args), =:tool-always= (matches any args), =:tool-deny= (always denies).
- =args-fingerprint=: Hash of args for =:exact-args= matching (via =fingerprint-args=).
- =decision= (Keyword): =:allow= or =:deny=.
******* register-permission-rule
#+begin_src lisp
  (register-permission-rule rule)
#+end_src

Register a =permission-rule=, maintaining priority order (highest first). If a rule with the same name already exists, it is replaced.

- =rule= (permission-rule): The rule to register.
******* unregister-permission-rule
#+begin_src lisp
  (unregister-permission-rule name)
#+end_src

Remove a permission rule by name.

- =name= (String): The name of the rule to remove.
******* list-permission-rules
#+begin_src lisp
  (list-permission-rules)
#+end_src

Return the list of all active permission rules, ordered by priority (highest first).
******* clear-session-overrides
#+begin_src lisp
  (clear-session-overrides)
#+end_src

Clear all session overrides.
******* fingerprint-args
#+begin_src lisp
  (fingerprint-args args)
#+end_src

Create a hash fingerprint of tool arguments for exact-match session overrides.

- =args=: The arguments plist to fingerprint.

Returns an integer hash.
******* resolve-permission
#+begin_src lisp
  (resolve-permission tool-name args)
#+end_src

Determine the permission decision for a tool call. Checks session overrides first (highest priority), then walks rules in priority order. Returns =:confirm= as the default if no rule matches.

- =tool-name= (String): The tool being called.
- =args= (Plist): The tool's arguments.

Returns =:allow=, =:deny=, or =:confirm=.
******* prompt-tool-permission
#+begin_src lisp
  (prompt-tool-permission tool-name args)
#+end_src

Present an interactive multi-option confirmation prompt to the user for a tool call. Options include allowing/denying once, always allowing the tool, always allowing the exact call, always denying, or showing tool details.

- =tool-name= (String): The tool requesting permission.
- =args= (Plist): The tool's arguments.

Returns =:allow= or =:deny=.
******* defperm (Macro)
#+begin_src lisp
  (defperm name (&key tool priority description source) &body body)
#+end_src

Define and register a named permission rule. The body is evaluated with =tool-name= (string) and =args= (plist) bound, and must return =:allow=, =:deny=, =:confirm=, or =:abstain=.

- =name= (Symbol): Name for the rule.
- =tool= (String or =:any=): Tool pattern to match.
- =priority= (Integer, default 0): Higher values are checked first.
- =description= (String): Human-readable description.
- =source= (Keyword, default =:user=): Origin — =:system=, =:user=, =:mode=, =:session=.

Example:
#+begin_src lisp
  (defperm allow-project-reads
    (:tool "read_file" :priority 50 :source :system
     :description "Auto-allow reading files within the project")
    (if (path-in-project? (getf args :path))
        :allow
        :abstain))
#+end_src
******* Built-in Predicates
******** path-in-project?
#+begin_src lisp
  (path-in-project? path)
#+end_src

Returns =T= if =path= resolves to within =*repo-root*=.
******** path-matches?
#+begin_src lisp
  (path-matches? path pattern)
#+end_src

Returns =T= if =path= matches the regex =pattern=.
******** path-is-readonly?
#+begin_src lisp
  (path-is-readonly? path)
#+end_src

Returns =T= if =path= is in a known read-only location (=node_modules/=, =.git/=, =__pycache__/=, etc.).
******** command-safe?
#+begin_src lisp
  (command-safe? command)
#+end_src

Returns =T= if =command= matches a registered safe-command pattern (e.g. =ls=, =git status=, =grep=).
******** command-destructive?
#+begin_src lisp
  (command-destructive? command)
#+end_src

Returns =T= if =command= matches known destructive patterns (e.g. =sudo=, =rm -rf /=, =dd=).
******** command-in-project?
#+begin_src lisp
  (command-in-project? command)
#+end_src

Returns =T= (always). Commands executed from the REPL run in =*repo-root*= by default.
******** args-match-pattern?
#+begin_src lisp
  (args-match-pattern? args pattern-alist)
#+end_src

Returns =T= if tool =args= match the given =pattern-alist=. Pattern values can be regex strings or exact values.

- =args= (Plist): The tool's arguments.
- =pattern-alist= (Alist): Pairs of =(keyword . pattern)=.
******* register-safe-command
#+begin_src lisp
  (register-safe-command pattern)
#+end_src

Add a regex pattern to the =*safe-command-patterns*= list. Commands matching any safe pattern are considered read-only.

- =pattern= (String): A regex pattern.
******* log-permission-decision
#+begin_src lisp
  (log-permission-decision tool-name args decision source)
#+end_src

Log a permission decision to =*permission-log*= for debugging. The log is trimmed to =*permission-log-max*= entries.

- =tool-name= (String): The tool that was checked.
- =args=: The tool's arguments.
- =decision= (Keyword): The decision (=:allow=, =:deny=, =:confirm=).
- =source= (String): The name of the rule or override that produced the decision.
******* /permissions (Command)
#+begin_src
  /permissions [clear|log|reset]
#+end_src

View and manage permission rules.
- No args: List all active rules and session overrides.
- =clear=: Clear session overrides.
- =log=: Show recent permission decisions.
- =reset=: Remove all non-system rules and clear session overrides.
******* /allow (Command)
#+begin_src
  /allow <tool_name>
#+end_src

Add a session override to always allow a tool for the current session.
******* /deny (Command)
#+begin_src
  /deny <tool_name>
#+end_src

Add a session override to always deny a tool for the current session.
******* Default Permission Rules
The following rules are registered by default at system startup:

| Priority | Name                             | Tool            | Behavior                                              |
|----------+----------------------------------+-----------------+-------------------------------------------------------|
|      100 | deny-dangerous-commands          | execute_command | Deny commands matching destructive patterns           |
|       50 | auto-allow-project-reads         | read_file       | Allow reading files within =*repo-root*=              |
|       40 | auto-allow-safe-project-commands | execute_command | Allow safe read-only commands in the project          |
|       10 | tool-default-permissions         | :any            | Fall through to the tool's own =:permissions= setting |
****** Agent Client Protocol (ACP)
The =acp.lisp= file implements the Agent Client Protocol (ACP) over JSON-RPC 2.0 via stdio. This allows Hactar to integrate deeply with editors and other clients, exposing capabilities and consuming client-provided capabilities.

ACP is the main structured editor-integration surface for modern Hactar clients. It supports:
- capability negotiation
- session lifecycle management
- streaming message chunks
- tool-call progress updates
- client-mediated permissions
- filesystem and terminal round-trips
******* Macros
******** defcapability
#+begin_src lisp
  (defmacro defcapability (name (&rest path) &body body))
#+end_src

Define an ACP agent capability.

- =name= (Symbol): Naming the capability (used for the handler function).
- =path= (List of Strings): The capability path, e.g. =("fs" "readTextFile")=.
- =body=: Can start with keyword options (=:description=, =:enabled=, =:permissions=, =:advertise=), followed by the handler implementation. The handler receives =(id params)= arguments.
******* Client Communication (Agent -> Client)
******** acp-call-client
#+begin_src lisp
  (acp-call-client method params &key (timeout 60))
#+end_src

Send a JSON-RPC request to the Client and wait for the response. Returns the result or signals an error on timeout.
******** acp-send-session-update
#+begin_src lisp
  (acp-send-session-update update)
#+end_src

Send a =session/update= notification to the Client. There are several helper functions that wrap this for specific update types:
- =(acp-send-agent-message-chunk text)=
- =(acp-send-user-message-chunk text)=
- =(acp-send-thought-chunk text)=
- =(acp-send-tool-call tool-call-id title kind status &key content locations raw-input)=
- =(acp-send-tool-call-update tool-call-id status &key content)=
******** acp-request-permission
#+begin_src lisp
  (acp-request-permission tool-name args tool-call-id)
#+end_src
Request permission from the Client for a tool call. Returns =:allow= or =:deny=.
******* Client Capabilities
******** acp-client-has-capability?
#+begin_src lisp
  (acp-client-has-capability? path)
#+end_src

Check if the Client advertised a capability at the given dotted path (e.g., ='("fs" "readTextFile")=).
******** Client Capability Wrappers
Hactar provides wrapper functions to easily invoke standard Client capabilities if they are available:
- =(acp-fs-read-text-file path &key line limit)=
- =(acp-fs-write-text-file path content)=
- =(acp-terminal-create command &key args env cwd output-byte-limit)=
- =(acp-terminal-output terminal-id)=
- =(acp-terminal-wait-for-exit terminal-id)=
- =(acp-terminal-kill terminal-id)=
- =(acp-terminal-release terminal-id)=
******* Core Functions
******** start-acp
#+begin_src lisp
  (start-acp)
#+end_src

Initialize and start the ACP stdio server. Enters the main JSON-RPC message loop.
****** Model Context Protocol (MCP)
The =mcp.lisp= file implements the Model Context Protocol (MCP) over JSON-RPC 2.0 via stdio. This allows Hactar to act as an MCP server, exposing its defined tools to MCP clients.
******* JSON-RPC Transport & Construction
******** mcp-write-message
#+begin_src lisp
  (mcp-write-message message)
#+end_src

Serialize an alist =message= as JSON and write to stdout as a single newline-delimited line.
******** mcp-read-message
#+begin_src lisp
  (mcp-read-message)
#+end_src

Read a single newline-delimited JSON-RPC message from stdin. Returns the parsed alist or =NIL= on EOF.
******** mcp-log
#+begin_src lisp
  (mcp-log fmt &rest args)
#+end_src

Log a message to stderr for debugging in MCP mode.
******** mcp-make-response
#+begin_src lisp
  (mcp-make-response id result)
#+end_src

Create a JSON-RPC 2.0 success response alist.
******** mcp-make-error-response
#+begin_src lisp
  (mcp-make-error-response id code message &optional data)
#+end_src

Create a JSON-RPC 2.0 error response alist.
******** mcp-make-notification
#+begin_src lisp
  (mcp-make-notification method params)
#+end_src

Create a JSON-RPC 2.0 notification alist (no id).
******* Tool Schema Conversion
******** tool-parameter-to-mcp-schema
#+begin_src lisp
  (tool-parameter-to-mcp-schema param)
#+end_src

Convert a =tool-parameter= to MCP/JSON Schema format.
******** tool-definition-to-mcp-schema
#+begin_src lisp
  (tool-definition-to-mcp-schema tool)
#+end_src

Convert a =tool-definition= to MCP tools/list format.
******* Method Handlers & Dispatch
******** mcp-handle-initialize
#+begin_src lisp
  (mcp-handle-initialize id params)
#+end_src

Handle the MCP initialize method.
******** mcp-handle-ping
#+begin_src lisp
  (mcp-handle-ping id params)
#+end_src

Handle the MCP ping method.
******** mcp-handle-tools-list
#+begin_src lisp
  (mcp-handle-tools-list id params)
#+end_src

Handle tools/list — return all defined tools in MCP schema format.
******** mcp-handle-tools-call
#+begin_src lisp
  (mcp-handle-tools-call id params)
#+end_src

Handle tools/call — execute a tool and return the result.
******** mcp-notify-tools-changed
#+begin_src lisp
  (mcp-notify-tools-changed)
#+end_src

Send a notifications/tools/list_changed notification to the client.
******** mcp-dispatch-message
#+begin_src lisp
  (mcp-dispatch-message msg)
#+end_src

Dispatch an incoming JSON-RPC message to the appropriate MCP handler.
******* Core Functions
******** mcp-main-loop
#+begin_src lisp
  (mcp-main-loop)
#+end_src

Main stdio loop for MCP mode. Reads JSON-RPC messages and dispatches them.
******** start-mcp
#+begin_src lisp
  (start-mcp)
#+end_src

Initialize and start the MCP stdio server.
******** mcp (Command)
#+begin_src lisp
  (define-sub-command mcp (args))
#+end_src

Start Hactar as a Model Context Protocol (MCP) server over stdio.
****** Lisp-RPC Mode
Lisp-RPC mode allows Hactar to expose a Lisp API surface to the LLM and evaluate Lisp forms returned by the LLM in a sandboxed environment. It also provides a standard output protocol for editor integration.

This mode is intentionally opinionated: the model is expected to return Lisp forms explicitly, and evaluation is constrained by a whitelist-based validator before any form is executed.
******* Core Concepts
- *Sandboxed Evaluation*: The LLM can emit Lisp forms inside =```lisp= or =<lisp>= blocks. These forms are read using a restricted readtable and validated against a whitelist of allowed symbols before evaluation.
- *API Registry*: Functions exposed to the LLM are defined using the =defapi= macro and stored in =*api-registry*=.
- *Standard Output Protocol*: When active, Hactar emits standard s-expressions to stdout (e.g., =(hactar-response "text")=) for easy parsing by editor clients.
******* Variables
- =*rpc-output-stream*=: When non-nil, =rpc-emit= writes to this stream instead of computing the output stream. Useful for testing.
- =*api-registry*=: Hash table of registered Lisp-RPC API functions. Key: string name, Value: =api-definition=.
- =*lisp-rpc-exposed-categories*=: List of API categories (keywords) or function names (symbols) to expose in the system prompt. =:all= means expose everything.
- =*lisp-rpc-eval-timeout*=: Maximum seconds for evaluating a single Lisp-RPC form.
- =*lisp-rpc-eval-log*=: Log of recent Lisp-RPC evaluations for debugging.
- =*lisp-rpc-eval-log-max*=: Maximum entries in the eval log.
- =*lisp-rpc-allowed-cl-symbols*=: Whitelist of CL symbols allowed in Lisp-RPC sandboxed evaluation.
- =*lisp-rpc-blocked-symbols*=: Symbols explicitly blocked from Lisp-RPC evaluation, even if they appear in CL.
- =*lisp-rpc-readtable*=: Restricted readtable for parsing Lisp-RPC forms from LLM output.
******* Structs
******** api-definition
#+begin_src lisp
  (make-api-definition :name :lambda-list :docstring :category :permissions :examples :dangerous :returns :side-effects :function)
#+end_src
Structure representing a registered Lisp-RPC API function.
******* Macros
******** defapi
#+begin_src lisp
  (defmacro defapi (name lambda-list &body body))
#+end_src

Define a Lisp-RPC API function.

- =name= (Symbol): Naming the function (interned in =HACTAR= package).
- =lambda-list= (List): Ordinary lambda list.
- =body=: Starts with a required docstring, followed by keyword options, then the implementation.

Keyword options:
- =:permissions= (=:confirm=, =:auto=, =:deny=): Permission level (default =:confirm=).
- =:category= (Keyword): Grouping for the prompt (e.g., =:filesystem=, =:context=).
- =:examples= (List): Quoted list of example calls shown to the LLM.
- =:dangerous= (Boolean): If =T=, always requires confirmation.
- =:returns= (String): Description of the return value.
- =:side-effects= (String): Description of side effects.
******* Protocol Emitters
These functions emit standard s-expressions to stdout for editor clients.

- =(rpc-emit form)=: Write a single s-expression to stdout and flush.
- =(rpc-hello version model)=: Emit =(hactar-hello ...)=.
- =(rpc-ready)=: Emit =(hactar-ready)=.
- =(rpc-response text)=: Emit =(hactar-response ...)=.
- =(rpc-status kind &rest args)=: Emit =(hactar-status ...)=.
- =(rpc-eval-result result form)=: Emit =(hactar-eval-result ...)=.
- =(rpc-eval-output output form)=: Emit =(hactar-eval-output ...)=.
- =(rpc-eval-error message form)=: Emit =(hactar-eval-error ...)=.
- =(rpc-error message)=: Emit =(hactar-error ...)=.
- =(rpc-warning message &rest details)=: Emit =(hactar-warning ...)=.
- =(rpc-cancelled)=: Emit =(hactar-cancelled)=.
- =(rpc-interrupted)=: Emit =(hactar-interrupted)=.
- =(rpc-exit &optional reason)=: Emit =(hactar-exit ...)=.
- =(rpc-model-changed name)=: Emit =(hactar-model-changed ...)=.
- =(rpc-model-not-found name)=: Emit =(hactar-model-not-found ...)=.
- =(rpc-history-compressed)=: Emit =(hactar-history-compressed)=.
- =(rpc-command-output text command)=: Emit =(hactar-command-output ...)=.
- =(rpc-permission-request tool args description options)=: Emit =(hactar-permission-request ...)=.
- =(rpc-stream-chunk chunk)=: Emit a streaming chunk of LLM response text.
- =(rpc-stream-end)=: Emit end-of-stream marker.
- =(rpc-event kind &rest data)=: Emit an extensible event form.
- =(rpc-log level message &rest data)=: Emit a log form.
******* Evaluation & Security
******** lisp-rpc-eval
#+begin_src lisp
  (lisp-rpc-eval form-or-string)
#+end_src
Evaluate a Lisp-RPC form in the sandboxed environment. Validates all symbols via a code walk before evaluation. Returns =(values result output-string error-string)=.
******** validate-lisp-rpc-form
#+begin_src lisp
  (validate-lisp-rpc-form form)
#+end_src
Walk a form tree and validate all symbols are allowed. Signals =lisp-rpc-security-error= if any disallowed symbol is found.
******** validate-lisp-rpc-quoted
#+begin_src lisp
  (validate-lisp-rpc-quoted form)
#+end_src
Validate a quoted form. Allows data but blocks function symbols.
******** lisp-rpc-symbol-allowed-p
#+begin_src lisp
  (lisp-rpc-symbol-allowed-p sym)
#+end_src
Check if a symbol is allowed in Lisp-RPC evaluation.
******** lisp-rpc-read-form
#+begin_src lisp
  (lisp-rpc-read-form string)
#+end_src
Read a single Lisp form from STRING using the restricted readtable.
******** extract-lisp-rpc-forms
#+begin_src lisp
  (extract-lisp-rpc-forms text)
#+end_src
Extract Lisp forms from LLM response text. Looks for =```lisp= fenced blocks and =<lisp>= tagged blocks.
******** lisp-rpc-process-response
#+begin_src lisp
  (lisp-rpc-process-response response-text)
#+end_src
Process an LLM response, extracting and evaluating any Lisp-RPC forms.
******* Editor Integration (Slynk)
******** lisp-rpc-prompt
#+begin_src lisp
  (lisp-rpc-prompt text &key model)
#+end_src
Send TEXT as a prompt to the LLM, streaming chunks to stdout via =rpc-stream-chunk=. Blocks until the response is complete.
******** lisp-rpc-get-state
#+begin_src lisp
  (lisp-rpc-get-state)
#+end_src
Return the current Hactar state as an alist for editor inspection.
******** lisp-rpc-execute-command
#+begin_src lisp
  (lisp-rpc-execute-command cmd-string)
#+end_src
Execute a slash command from the editor and return output as a string.
******** lisp-rpc-available-models
#+begin_src lisp
  (lisp-rpc-available-models)
#+end_src
Return a list of available model names.
******** lisp-rpc-current-model
#+begin_src lisp
  (lisp-rpc-current-model)
#+end_src
Return the current model name or nil.
******** lisp-rpc-chat-history
#+begin_src lisp
  (lisp-rpc-chat-history)
#+end_src
Return the current chat history.
******** lisp-rpc-respond-permission
#+begin_src lisp
  (lisp-rpc-respond-permission response)
#+end_src
Respond to a pending permission request from the editor.
******** lisp-rpc-pending-permission
#+begin_src lisp
  (lisp-rpc-pending-permission)
#+end_src
Return the current pending permission request plist, or nil.
******** lisp-rpc-main-loop
#+begin_src lisp
  (lisp-rpc-main-loop)
#+end_src
Main loop for Lisp-RPC mode. Reads forms from stdin and evaluates them.
******* Built-in API Functions
These functions are exposed to the LLM via the =defapi= macro.

- =(read-file path)=: Read the contents of a file at PATH (relative to project root). Also adds the file to context.
- =(write-file path content)=: Write CONTENT to file at PATH (relative to project root). Creates directories as needed.
- =(replace-in-file path search replace)=: Replace the first occurrence of SEARCH text with REPLACE text in file at PATH.
- =(file-exists-p path)=: Check if a file exists at PATH (relative to project root).
- =(list-directory path)=: List files in directory at PATH (relative to project root).
- =(add-to-context path)=: Add a file to the chat context window.
- =(drop-from-context path)=: Remove a file from the chat context window.
- =(context-files)=: List all files currently in the chat context.
- =(search-project query)=: Search project files for QUERY using ripgrep. Returns matching filenames.
- =(sh command)=: Execute a shell command in the project directory. Returns stdout + stderr.
- =(sh-read command)=: Execute a read-only shell command (ls, cat, grep, etc.). Auto-approved.
- =(git-diff)=: Show the current git diff (unstaged changes).
- =(git-status)=: Show git status.
- =(git-commit-changes message)=: Stage all changes and commit with MESSAGE.
******* Commands
- =/lisp-rpc [status|eval|log|expose|api]=: Manage Lisp-RPC mode.
- =/ls-rpc=: Emit the hello protocol message.
****** BOT Entity System
The BOT (Behavior-Object-Tags) Entity System provides an Entity-Component-System architecture for Hactar. It allows defining abstract entities (like routes, models, components), attaching behaviors via tags, and providing LLM instructions via skills.
******* Core Concepts
- *Entities*: Abstract definitions of project components (e.g., =frameworkroute=, =model=). Defined with =defentity=.
- *Tags*: Groupings of behaviors that can be applied to entities (e.g., =:api=, =:protected=). Defined with =deftag=.
- *Behaviors*: Composable units of functionality attached to entities via tags. They can provide lifecycle hooks, validation, and rules. Defined with =defbehavior=.
- *Skills*: Instruction sets loaded into the LLM context during entity operations. Defined with =defskill=.
- *Implementations*: Framework-specific concrete implementations of an entity type (e.g., an Express.js route vs a Django route).
******* Macros
******** defentity
#+begin_src lisp
  (defentity name description &body body)
#+end_src

Define a base entity type and auto-generate the =def<entity>= macro for framework-specific implementations. It also automatically generates CRUD commands (e.g., =/<name>.create=) and CLI subcommands.

- =name= (Symbol): The entity type name.
- =description= (String): Human-readable description.
- =body=: Keyword arguments including =:schema=, =:behaviors=, =:commands=, =:storage=, and =:searchable=.
******** defskill
#+begin_src lisp
  (defskill name description &body body)
#+end_src

Define a skill that provides instructions to the LLM.

- =name= (Keyword): The skill name.
- =description= (String): Human-readable description.
- =body=: Keyword arguments =:instructions=, =:rules=, and =:examples=.
******** defbehavior
#+begin_src lisp
  (defbehavior name description &body body)
#+end_src

Define a composable behavior that can attach to entities via tags.

- =name= (Symbol): The behavior name.
- =description= (String): Human-readable description.
- =body=: Keyword arguments for hooks (=:before-create=, =:after-create=, etc.), =:tags=, =:skill=, =:rule=, =:generator=, and =:validator=.
******** deftag
#+begin_src lisp
  (deftag name description &body body)
#+end_src

Define a tag that groups behaviors.

- =name= (Keyword): The tag name.
- =description= (String): Human-readable description.
- =body=: Keyword arguments =:behaviors=, =:inherits=, =:requires=, and =:skills=.
******** defentity-recipe
#+begin_src lisp
  (defentity-recipe name description &body body)
#+end_src

Define a multi-entity recipe.

- =name= (Symbol): The recipe name.
- =description= (String): Human-readable description.
- =body=: Keyword arguments =:creates=, =:installs=, and =:configures=.
******* Entity CRUD Operations
******** entity/create
#+begin_src lisp
  (entity/create entity-type name &rest args)
#+end_src

Create an entity instance using the best available implementation. Loads skills, activates behaviors, validates, and runs hooks.
******** entity/list
#+begin_src lisp
  (entity/list entity-type &rest args)
#+end_src

List entities using the best available implementation or fall back to in-memory instances.
******** entity/update
#+begin_src lisp
  (entity/update entity-type name &rest args)
#+end_src

Update an entity using the best available implementation.
******** entity/delete
#+begin_src lisp
  (entity/delete entity-type name &rest args)
#+end_src

Delete an entity using the best available implementation.
******* Built-in Entity Types
- =frameworkroute=: Represents an HTTP endpoint or page route.
- =model=: A data model or schema definition.
- =component=: A UI component definition.
- =lib=: A shared library or utility module.
******* Built-in Tags
- =:api=: Tag for API endpoints.
- =:crud=: Tag for full CRUD entities.
- =:protected=: Tag for routes requiring authentication.
- =:public=: Tag for publicly accessible routes.
- =:authenticated=: Inherits from =:protected=.
****** markdown
Markdown parsing stuff lives in markdown.lisp
******* Core Functions
******** =get-all-md-src-blocks=
#+begin_src lisp
  (get-all-md-src-blocks markdown-string)
#+end_src

Return all Markdown fenced code blocks with languages and contents.
******** =render-markdown-to-html=
#+begin_src lisp
  (render-markdown-to-html markdown-string)
#+end_src

Render Markdown to HTML.
******** =insert-md-sibling=
#+begin_src lisp
  (insert-md-sibling node sibling)
#+end_src

Insert a Markdown sibling node.
******** =insert-md-child=
#+begin_src lisp
  (insert-md-child node child)
#+end_src

Append a Markdown child node.
****** Context Preset System
The =preset.lisp= file provides a system for defining reusable context configurations (presets) and capturing session states (snapshots). Presets bundle files, docs, rules, and skills, while snapshots allow saving and restoring the exact context state (including history).
******* Structs
******** preset
#+begin_src lisp
  (make-preset :name :description :files :docs :rules :skills :requires-stack :setup-fn :teardown-fn :extends :active-p :source-file)
#+end_src
A reusable context configuration.
******** context-snapshot
#+begin_src lisp
  (make-context-snapshot :name :timestamp :description :files :images :docs-context :errors-context :active-rules-text :active-presets :chat-history-p :chat-history)
#+end_src
A saved state of the context that can be restored.
******* Macros
******** defpreset
#+begin_src lisp
  (defmacro defpreset (name description &body body))
#+end_src
Define a reusable context preset. Accepts keywords like =:files=, =:docs=, =:rules=, =:skills=, =:requires-stack=, =:setup=, =:teardown=, and =:extends=.
******* Core Functions
******** preset/load
#+begin_src lisp
  (preset/load name &key quiet)
#+end_src
Load a preset by name, resolving inheritance, checking requirements, executing setup hooks, and adding its files/docs/skills to the context.
******** preset/unload
#+begin_src lisp
  (preset/unload name &key quiet)
#+end_src
Unload a preset, running teardown hooks and removing its files from the context.
******** snapshot/save
#+begin_src lisp
  (snapshot/save name &key description include-history)
#+end_src
Save the current context state (files, docs, rules, active presets, and optionally chat history) to disk as a JSON snapshot.
******** snapshot/restore
#+begin_src lisp
  (snapshot/restore name)
#+end_src
Restore context from a snapshot, clearing the current context state and replacing it with the snapshot's state.
******* Commands
- =/preset [name]=: Load a preset or list available presets.
- =/preset.load <name>=: Load a preset by name.
- =/preset.unload [name]=: Unload specific or all presets.
- =/preset.list=: List available presets with details.
- =/preset.show <name>=: Show details of a specific preset.
- =/preset.active=: Show currently active presets.
- =/preset.save <name> [description]=: Save current context as a new preset.
- =/preset.reload [name]=: Reload a preset or all active presets.
- =/snapshot [name]=: List snapshots or save current context.
- =/snapshot.save <name> [--history] [--description "desc"]=: Save current context as a snapshot.
- =/snapshot.restore <name>=: Restore context from a snapshot.
- =/snapshot.delete <name>=: Delete a snapshot.
- =/snapshot.list=: List all snapshots with details.

CLI Sub-commands:
- =hactar preset list=
- =hactar preset load <name>=
- =hactar preset show <name>=
****** Session Management
The =session.lisp= file provides a system for capturing, saving, and restoring the full state of a Hactar instance. Sessions are persisted as human-readable Lisp forms, allowing users to switch contexts, resume previous work, and maintain project-local or global session histories.

This is distinct from snapshots in =preset.lisp=. Snapshots focus on context state; sessions aim to restore the whole working session, including models, chat history, active presets, flags, and context selections.
******* Structs
******** hactar-session
#+begin_src lisp
  (make-hactar-session :name :description :timestamp :repo-root :project-name :model-name :cheap-model :docs-meta-model :files :images :docs-context :errors-context :chat-history :stack :active-presets :active-rules :git-autocommit :tool-use-enabled :metadata)
#+end_src
A saved Hactar session state representing everything needed to completely restore a working environment.
******* Core Functions
******** session/save
#+begin_src lisp
  (session/save name &key description global)
#+end_src
Save the current Hactar state as a named session. If =global= is =T=, it saves to the global sessions directory instead of project-local.
******** session/load
#+begin_src lisp
  (session/load name &key global quiet)
#+end_src
Load and restore a session by name. Clears the current state and completely replaces it with the session's state. Searches project-local first, then global.
******** session/delete
#+begin_src lisp
  (session/delete name &key global)
#+end_src
Delete a session file.
******** session/list
#+begin_src lisp
  (session/list)
#+end_src
List all available sessions with summary info (name, model, file count, message count).
******** session/show
#+begin_src lisp
  (session/show name)
#+end_src
Show detailed information about a session without loading it into the active state.
******** session/auto-save
#+begin_src lisp
  (session/auto-save)
#+end_src
Auto-save current session if the feature is enabled. Usually called on exit.
******** session/auto-restore
#+begin_src lisp
  (session/auto-restore)
#+end_src
Auto-restore the previous session if auto-save is enabled and an autosave exists.
******* Commands
- =/session [name]=: List all sessions or load a session by name.
- =/session.save <name> [--global] [--description "desc"]=: Save current state as a session.
- =/session.load <name> [--global]=: Load and restore a session.
- =/session.list=: List all available sessions.
- =/session.show <name>=: Show details of a session without loading it.
- =/session.delete <name> [--global]=: Delete a session.
- =/session.auto [on|off]=: Toggle auto-save session on exit.

CLI Sub-commands:
- =hactar session list=
- =hactar session save <name> [--description "..."]=
- =hactar session load <name>=
- =hactar session show <name>=
- =hactar session delete <name>=
**** nhooks
The =nhooks= package implements a publish/subscribe hook system allowing different parts of the application to react to events. It is a slightly modified copy of the =nhooks= library developed by the Nyxt browser team.

A hook is an instance of the =nhooks:hook= class. Typing in hooks ensures that their handlers accept the correct argument types and return the correct value types.
***** Variables
- =*hook*=: The default hook instance or dynamic variable used for hook operations.
***** Classes
****** handler
Wraps a handler function with extra metadata for identification and comparison.

- Slots:
  - =name=: Symbol naming the handler. Defaults to the function name if it is named.
  - =description=: Text description.
  - =fn=: The actual handler function.
  - =place=: If a setter, describes the slot or place being set.
  - =value=: If a setter, the value to set.
****** hook
The base class for hooks.

- Slots:
  - =handler-type=: Expected function type of handlers.
  - =handlers-alist=: Alist of =(handler . enable-p)= representing registered handlers and their active states.
  - =handlers=: List of active handler functions.
  - =disabled-handlers=: List of disabled handler functions.
  - =combination=: Function or symbol managing how results from handlers are combined.
***** Hook Combinations
- =default-combine-hook=: Returns a list of results from all enabled handlers.
- =combine-hook-until-failure=: Runs handlers until one returns =nil=.
- =combine-hook-until-success=: Runs handlers and returns the first non-nil result.
- =combine-composed-hook=: Composes handlers so the output of one is passed to the next.
***** Hook Operations
- =(add-hook hook handler &key append)=: Registers a handler.
- =(remove-hook hook handler-or-name)=: Removes a handler.
- =(run-hook hook &rest args)=: Runs all enabled handlers on the hook.
- =(run-hooks &rest hooks)=: Runs multiple hooks sequentially.
- =(run-hook-with-args-until-failure hook &rest args)=: Runs handlers on =hook= with =args= until one returns =nil=.
- =(run-hook-with-args-until-success hook &rest args)=: Runs handlers on =hook= with =args= and returns the first non-nil result.
- =(disable-hook hook &rest handlers)=: Disables specified handlers.
- =(enable-hook hook &rest handlers)=: Enables specified handlers.
- =(define-hook hook-type name &key object handlers disabled-handlers combination)=: Defines a globally-accessible hook.
- =(find-hook name &optional object)=: Looks up a global hook.
- =(define-hook-type name type &optional documentation)=: Macro to define a new subclass of =hook= with a specific =handler-type=.
- =(find-handler name hook)=: Finds a handler by name on the given hook.
- =(with-disable-handler-restart handler hook &body body)=: Establishes a restart to disable a failing handler.
***** Pre-generated Hook Types
- =hook-void=: Hook type for functions accepting no arguments.
- =hook-string->string=: Hook type for functions mapping string to string.
- =hook-number->number=: Hook type for functions mapping number to number.
- =hook-any=: Hook type for functions accepting any arguments.
***** Convenience Macros
- =(on hook args &body body)=: Attaches an anonymous handler to a hook.
- =(once-on hook args &body body)=: Attaches an anonymous handler that runs exactly once and then removes itself.
- =(wait-on hook args &body body)=: Blocks until the hook is triggered, returning the evaluation of `body`.
**** llm
Hactar uses a custom rolled lib called =llm= for abstracting over LLM APIs. Supports OpenAI, Anthropic, Google Gemini, Ollama, and OpenRouter. It supports streaming and non-streaming responses, vision + image capabilities, and tool use.
***** Configuration
****** API Keys
API keys are loaded from environment variables.

- =*openai-api-key*=: Loaded from =OPENAI_API_KEY=.
- =*anthropic-api-key*=: Loaded from =ANTHROPIC_API_KEY=.
- =*gemini-api-key*=: Loaded from =GEMINI_API_KEY=.
- =*openrouter-api-key*=: Loaded from =OPENROUTER_API_KEY=.
****** Special Variables
- =*read-timeout*=: (Default: =120=) The timeout in seconds for HTTP
  requests to the LLM providers.
- =*debug*=: (Default: =nil=) When =T=, enables debug logging to
  standard output.
- =*debug-stream*=: (Default: =nil=) When set to a stream, detailed
  debug logs are written to it.
- =*default-system-prompt*=: (Default: ="You are a helpful assistant."=)
  The default system prompt used if no other is provided.
****** Functions
******* dump-api-keys
#+begin_src lisp
  (dump-api-keys)
#+end_src

Returns a string containing the status of the loaded API keys. Useful for debugging.
***** core API
****** complete
#+begin_src lisp
  (complete type messages &rest args &key (max-context 32000) images tools &allow-other-keys)
#+end_src

Dispatches a completion request to the appropriate provider specific function.

- =type=: A keyword specifying the provider. One of =:openai=,
  =:ollama=, =:anthropic=, =:openrouter=, or =:gemini=.
- =messages=: A list of message alists, e.g.,
  ='(((:role . "user") (:content . "Hello")))=.
- =&key=:
  - =stream= (Boolean): If =T=, the function returns an
    =llm-stream-reader= object for streaming the response. If =NIL=
    (default), it returns the full response text.
  - =model= (String): The specific model name to use (e.g.,
    ="gpt-4o-mini"=).
  - =system-prompt= (String): A system prompt to override the default.
  - =max-tokens= (Integer): The maximum number of tokens to generate in
    the response.
  - =max-context= (Integer): The context window size for the model.
  - =images= (List): A list of image plists for vision-capable models.
    Each plist should contain =:base64-data= and =:mime-type=.
  - =tools= (List): A list of tool definitions for the LLM to use.

*Return Value (Non-streaming):* Returns three values:
1. =response-text=
(String): The content of the assistant's response.
1. =tool-calls-list=
(List): A list of tool calls made by the model, or =NIL=.
1. =full-message-history= (List): The complete list of messages sent to and
received from the API.

*Return Value (Streaming):* Returns two values:
1. An =llm-stream-reader= instance.
2. The list of messages that were sent to the API.
***** Provider Specific Functions
****** openai-complete
Signature:

#+begin_src lisp
  (openai-complete messages
                  &key
                  (api-key *openai-api-key*)
                  (model "gpt-4o-mini")
                  (endpoint "https://api.openai.com/v1/chat/completions")
                  (system-prompt *default-system-prompt*)
                  (max-tokens 1024)
                  (max-context 32000) ; ignored
                  (stream nil)
                  (response-format nil)
                  (images nil)
                  (tools nil)
                  (extra-headers nil)
                  &allow-other-keys)
#+end_src
- Prepares messages and inserts a =system= message (if not present)
- If =images= are provided:
  - The last user message becomes a list of content parts:
    - First: text part =((:type . "text") (:content . user-text))=
    - Then: one or more image parts with data URIs via =image_url=
- Builds OpenAI Chat Completions payload:
  - =:model=, =:messages=, ="max_tokens"=, =:stream=
  - Optional ="response_format"= e.g., =("type" . "json_object")=
  - Optional =:tools= and =:tool_choice "auto"=
- Auth header: =Authorization: Bearer <api-key>=

*Returns*
- Streaming: =(llm-stream-reader processed-messages)=
- Non-streaming: =(content tool-calls updated-history)=
******* Examples
Non streaming:

#+begin_src lisp
  (multiple-value-bind (text tool-calls history)
      (openai-complete
       "Write a haiku about the moon."
       :api-key (uiop:getenv "OPENAI_API_KEY")
       :model "gpt-4o-mini"
       :max-tokens 200)
    (declare (ignore tool-calls history))
    (format t "~A~%" text))
#+end_src

With images:

#+begin_src lisp
  (let* ((imgs (list '((:base64-data . "BASE64...") (:mime-type . "image/png"))))
         (msgs '(((:role . "user") (:content . "Describe this image and its mood.")))))
    (openai-complete msgs :images imgs))
#+end_src

Streaming:

#+begin_src lisp
  (let ((prompt "Stream a short poem about the ocean."))
    (multiple-value-bind (reader history)
        (llm:openai-complete
         prompt
         :model "gpt-4o-mini"
         :stream t
         ;; Optional: explicitly pass API key; by default it uses *openai-api-key* from env
         ;; :api-key (uiop:getenv "OPENAI_API_KEY")
         )
      (declare (ignore history))
      (unwind-protect
           (loop for chunk = (llm:read-next-chunk reader)
                 while chunk do
                   (princ chunk)           ; print as it streams
                   (force-output))
        (when reader
          (llm:close-reader reader)))))
#+end_src
****** ollama-complete
Signature:
#+begin_src lisp
  (ollama-complete messages
                   &key
                   (model "llama3")
                   (endpoint "http://localhost:11434/api/chat")
                   (system-prompt *default-system-prompt*)
                   (stream nil)
                   (response-format nil)
                   (max-tokens 1024) ; use via options.num_predict if enabled
                   (max-context 32000) ; sent as options.num_ctx
                   (images nil)
                   (tools nil)
                   (extra-headers nil)
                   &allow-other-keys)
#+end_src

- Prepares messages and inserts a =system= message (if not present)
- If =images= are provided:
  - The last user message gets an additional key =:images= with a list of base64 strings
- Payload:
  - ="model"=, ="messages"=, ="stream"=
  - ="options"= map:
    - ="num_ctx"= set from =:max-context=
    - Optionally enable ="num_predict"= if you uncomment it in code
  - Optional ="format"= from =:response-format= (e.g., ="json"=)
  - Optional =:tools= forwarded (provider support may vary)
- No auth header by default (local server)

*Returns*:
- Streaming: =(llm-stream-reader processed-messages)=
- Non-streaming: =(content nil updated-history)=
  - =tool-calls= is currently =nil=
****** Examples
non-streaming:
#+begin_src lisp
  (let* ((imgs (list '((:base64-data . "BASE64...") (:mime-type . "image/png"))))
         (msgs '(((:role . "user") (:content . "Describe what you see.")))))
    (ollama-complete msgs :images imgs))
#+end_src

Streaming:

#+begin_src lisp
  (let ((prompt "Stream a short poem about mountain winds."))
    (multiple-value-bind (reader history)
        (llm:ollama-complete
         prompt
         :model "llama3"
         :endpoint "http://localhost:11434/api/chat"
         :stream t)
      (declare (ignore history))
      (unwind-protect
           (loop for chunk = (llm:read-next-chunk reader)
                 while chunk do
                   (princ chunk)
                   (force-output))
        (when reader
          (llm:close-reader reader)))))
#+end_src
****** anthropic-complete
Signature:

#+begin_src lisp
  (anthropic-complete messages
                      &key
                      (api-key *anthropic-api-key*)
                      (model "claude-3-haiku-20240307")
                      (endpoint "https://api.anthropic.com/v1/messages")
                      (system-prompt *default-system-prompt*)
                      (max-tokens 1024)
                      (max-context 32000) ; ignored
                      (stream nil)
                      (images nil)
                      (tools nil)
                      (extra-headers nil)
                      &allow-other-keys)
#+end_src

- Prepares messages WITHOUT auto-inserting a =system= message
  - If =system-prompt= non-empty, it is sent via the top-level ="system"= payload field
- If =images= are provided:
  - The last user message content becomes a sequence of blocks:
    - One or more image blocks: =(:type "image")= with base64 source
    - Followed by a text block: =(:type "text")= with user text
- Payload includes:
  - ="model"=, ="messages"=, ="max_tokens"=, ="stream"=
  - Optional ="system"= when present
  - Optional =:tools= and ="tool_choice" . (:type . "auto")=
- Headers:
  - ="x-api-key"=, ="anthropic-version"= "2023-06-01"
  - ="anthropic-beta"= "tools-2024-04-04" (required for tools)

*Returns*:
- Streaming: =(llm-stream-reader processed-messages)=
- Non-streaming: =(content tool-calls updated-history)=
  - =tool-calls=: content blocks of type ="tool_use"=, if any
******* Examples
non-streaming:
#+begin_src lisp
  (multiple-value-bind (text tool-calls history)
      (anthropic-complete
       '(((:role . "user") (:content . "Summarize the key points of the Agile Manifesto.")))
       :api-key (uiop:getenv "ANTHROPIC_API_KEY")
       :model "claude-3-haiku-20240307"
       :max-tokens 300)
    (declare (ignore tool-calls history))
    (format t "~A~%" text))
#+end_src

Streaming:

#+begin_src lisp
  (let ((prompt "Stream a short poem about autumn leaves."))
    (multiple-value-bind (reader history)
        (llm:anthropic-complete
         prompt
         :model "claude-3-haiku-20240307"
         :stream t
         ;; Optional: explicitly pass API key; by default it uses *anthropic-api-key* from env
         ;; :api-key (uiop:getenv "ANTHROPIC_API_KEY")
         )
      (declare (ignore history))
      (unwind-protect
           (loop for chunk = (llm:read-next-chunk reader)
                 while chunk do
                   (princ chunk)
                   (force-output))
        (when reader
          (llm:close-reader reader)))))
#+end_src
****** openrouter-complete
Signature:

#+begin_src lisp
  (openrouter-complete messages
                       &key
                       (api-key *openrouter-api-key*)
                       (model "mistralai/mistral-7b-instruct:free")
                       (endpoint "https://openrouter.ai/api/v1/chat/completions")
                       (system-prompt *default-system-prompt*)
                       (max-tokens 1024)
                       (max-context 32000) ; ignored
                       (stream nil)
                       (response-format nil)
                       (images nil)
                       (tools nil)
                       (extra-headers nil)
                       &allow-other-keys)
#+end_src

- Same message/image handling as OpenAI (OpenRouter uses OpenAI-compatible format)
- Payload fields parallel OpenAI:
  - ="max_tokens"=, ="response_format"=, =:tools=, =:tool_choice "auto"=
- Headers:
  - =Authorization: Bearer <api-key>=
  - Optional recommended headers (uncomment in code): HTTP-Referer, X-Title

*Returns*:
- Streaming: =(llm-stream-reader processed-messages)=
- Non-streaming: =(content tool-calls updated-history)=
******* Examples
Non-streaming:

#+begin_src lisp
  (openrouter-complete
   '(((:role . "user") (:content . "List three creative uses for paperclips.")))
   :api-key (uiop:getenv "OPENROUTER_API_KEY")
   :model "meta-llama/llama-3.1-8b-instruct")
#+end_src

Streaming:

#+begin_src lisp
  (let ((prompt "Stream a short poem about sunrise."))
    (multiple-value-bind (reader history)
        (llm:openrouter-complete
         prompt
         :model "mistralai/mistral-7b-instruct:free"
         :stream t
         ;; Optional: explicitly pass API key; by default it uses *openrouter-api-key* from env
         ;; :api-key (uiop:getenv "OPENROUTER_API_KEY")
         ;; Optional: send recommended headers
         ;; :extra-headers '(("HTTP-Referer" . "https://your.app/")
         ;;                  ("X-Title" . "your-app-name"))
         )
      (declare (ignore history))
      (unwind-protect
           (loop for chunk = (llm:read-next-chunk reader)
                 while chunk do
                   (princ chunk)
                   (force-output))
        (when reader
          (llm:close-reader reader)))))
#+end_src
****** gemini-complete
Signature:

#+begin_src lisp
  (gemini-complete messages
                   &key
                   (api-key *gemini-api-key*)
                   (model "gemini-1.5-flash")
                   (endpoint "https://generativelanguage.googleapis.com/v1beta/models")
                   (system-prompt *default-system-prompt*)
                   (max-tokens 2048)
                   (stream nil)
                   (max-context 32000) ; ignored
                   (images nil)
                   (tools nil)
                   (extra-headers nil)
                   &allow-other-keys)
#+end_src

- Prepares messages WITHOUT auto-inserting a =system= message
- Converts messages to Gemini’s =contents= format:
  - Each message becomes =(("role" . "user"|"model") ("parts" . #(...)))=
  - Role mapping: "assistant" => "model", all others => "user"
  - Each parts vector starts with a text part =(("text" . content))=
- If =images= are provided:
  - For the LAST user message only, prepends one or more =inline_data= parts:
    - =(("inline_data" . (("mime_type" . ...) ("data" . base64))))=
  - Text part follows the image parts
- System prompt:
  - Sent via top-level ="system_instruction"= with =parts= vector
- Generation config:
  - Sent via ="generationConfig" => ("maxOutputTokens" . max-tokens)
- Endpoint/action:
  - Non-streaming: =.../<model>:generateContent?key=<API_KEY>=
  - Streaming: =.../<model>:streamGenerateContent?key=<API_KEY>&alt=sse=
- Content-Type header: ="application/json"=

*Returns*:
- Streaming: =(llm-stream-reader processed-messages)=
- Non-streaming: =(content function-calls updated-history)=
  - =function-calls=: extracted from parts with ="function_call"=, if any

Refer to the =llm:complete= documentation for common keyword arguments.
******* Examples
non-streaming:
#+begin_src lisp
  (multiple-value-bind (text calls history)
      (gemini-complete
       '(((:role . "user") (:content . "Explain quantum entanglement like I am five.")))
       :api-key (uiop:getenv "GEMINI_API_KEY")
       :model "gemini-1.5-flash"
       :max-tokens 256)
    (declare (ignore calls history))
    (format t "~A~%" text))
#+end_src

Streaming:
#+begin_src lisp

  (let ((prompt "Stream a short poem about starlight."))
    (multiple-value-bind (reader history)
        (llm:gemini-complete
         prompt
         :model "gemini-1.5-flash"
         :stream t
         ;; Optional: explicitly pass API key; by default it uses *gemini-api-key* from env
         ;; :api-key (uiop:getenv "GEMINI_API_KEY")
         )
      (declare (ignore history))
      (unwind-protect
           (loop for chunk = (llm:read-next-chunk reader)
                 while chunk do
                   (princ chunk)
                   (force-output))
        (when reader
          (llm:close-reader reader)))))
#+end_src
***** Streaming API
When =stream= is =T= in a completion call, the API returns a stream reader object to consume the response in chunks.
****** llm-stream-reader
A structure representing an active LLM stream. It is not meant to be instantiated directly by the user.

- =http-stream=: The underlying network stream.
- =provider=: The provider keyword (e.g., =:openai=).
- =closed-p=: A boolean indicating if the stream is closed.
- =tool-call-buffer=: Internal buffer for assembling tool calls.
****** read-next-chunk
#+begin_src lisp
  (read-next-chunk reader)
#+end_src

Reads the next available text chunk from the =llm-stream-reader= instance.

- =reader=: An =llm-stream-reader= object.

*Return Value:*
- A string containing the next piece of the response.
- =NIL= if the stream is finished.
****** close-reader
#+begin_src lisp
  (close-reader reader)
#+end_src

Manually closes the stream reader and its underlying network connection. This is called automatically when the stream ends.
****** llm-stream-reader-closed-p
#+begin_src lisp
  (llm-stream-reader-closed-p reader)
#+end_src

Returns =T= if the stream reader is closed, =NIL= otherwise.
****** llm-stream-reader-provider
#+begin_src lisp
  (llm-stream-reader-provider reader)
#+end_src

Returns the provider keyword (e.g., =:openai=) for the given stream reader.
***** Embeddings
****** ollama-embed
#+begin_src lisp
  (ollama-embed text &key model endpoint extra-headers)
#+end_src

Generates a vector embedding for the given text using an Ollama-compatible API.

- =text= (String): The input text to embed.
- =&key=:
  - =model= (String): The name of the embedding model to use (default:
    ="nomic-embed-text"=).
  - =endpoint= (String): The API endpoint (default:
    ="http://localhost:11434/api/embeddings"=).

*Return Value:*
- A list of numbers representing the embedding vector.
- =NIL= on error.
***** Provider Specific Functions (Additional)
****** copilot-complete

  (copilot-complete messages &key (token *github-copilot-token*) (model "gpt-4o") (stream nil) (max-tokens 1024) &allow-other-keys)
#+end_src

Completes a prompt using the GitHub Copilot API.
